電影專刊

美國製片家的大胆 323

— 羅浮

書於（影片·娜娜）觀後

有一個古代哲學者論及愛波羅（Ａｐｏｌｌｏ）的時候，他說：（愛波羅是一個音樂的神，同時也是一個　手，我愛他的歌，但是我怕他的箭！）看完了（影片，娜娜），第一個浮上心來的印象，就是這樣的一個使人苦笑的聯想。

假使你要在（電影，娜娜）裏面看到一些第三共和制時代的法蘭西社會的情形，或者要在影片裏面觀察一些自然主義作家愛彌爾，左拉筆下所描寫的女伶（娜娜）的波蘭重疊的生涯，那末你的希望是多餘的。更進一步，假使你要從這影片裏面看到一些這位具有强烈的正義感的作者能描出的對於當時貴族資產階級之腐敗的暴露乃至對於當時社會不正的批判，那末你的期待是否定的，（影片，娜娜一和（小說，娜娜）並没有血統的，遺傳的關係，原作對於電影，祇是一個Ｓｕｇｇｅｓｔｉｏｎ，美國的電影製作者薩繆，高爾文（ＳａｍｕｅｌＧｏｌｄｗｙｎ）用着美國待有的大胆的旁若無人的態度，毫不客氣地從法國自然主義作家的作品裏面奪取了他所歡喜的（歌）和避開了他所害怕的（箭）！

用和左拉同時代的偉大的批評家弗朗志，梅林格的話來講（左拉是）一個不能打開時代之深奥的秘密的思想家，是一個美學的尺度下的不完全的詩人，但是在他的才能和勸奮，在他的公正與勇敢，他是一個充分地有權利可以和他台洛，藍幸，羅騷，和伏德爾並肩的戰士！）在他的作品裏面，他不足的地描寫了當時的支配階級，鞭責了都市和農材商人階級的貪慾和反動，暴露了股票商人和宗敎業者的欺瞞和犯罪，更進一步，他還探究了現象和原因間的關聯，而指摘了將要到來的革命。這些，在高爾文眼中，無疑地都是可怕的（箭），銳利的（箭）。

但是，一方面，左拉是一個Ｌａｍｂｒｏｓｏ流的俗學的宿命論者，他不能打開時代的深奥的秘密，不能從他的𤍠烈地探究着的科學的方法，獲得一個對於社會組織之轉化的必然展望，他祇是借用了當時科學家們𤍠心地議論着的關於遺傳和環境的原理，用他可驚地眞摯和細密的手法，描寫了當時社會的一切病態的現象，絢爛，華奢，淫糜，和病態的妖麗。這是自然主義詩人的（歌），一種可以使爛熟了的世紀末的市民和電影製作家上歡喜的（歌）。

採取了這些派生的現象的描寫，和剽竊了（娜娜）這個逗人遐想的名字，而在巨萬的製作費和巨萬的宣傳費之下產生出來的，就是洗凈一切（左拉風）的幸辣和穢臭，而再加了一些濃烈的（仲馬風）的哀愁和傷感的（娜娜）的影片！

的確，這是一個戰爭和革命的時代。十九世紀七十年代的淫糜爛熟了的（娜娜），到二十世紀的四十年代也會變成國家主義的勇士，廳着窗外的（到伯林去）的呼聲，而在臨死時發出了（法蘭西需要你！）的口號！這是以杜萊浮士事件聞名的左拉的作品？丨這已經是（苦笑以上）的事了。

除出安娜史丹的卓越的演技之外，可以推賞的祇是薩繆，高爾文的那種美國商人特有的大膽的旁若無人製片方針和衛拉·麥克的（ＷｉｌｌａｒｄＭａｃｋ）的勇敢的Ａｄａｐｔａｔｉｏｎ而已。

觀衆意見

貞節坊下的血 324

— 深翁

觀（良宵）後有感

在這新舊過度的時代中，死掉丈夫的女子，究竟應不應該替丈夫守節，是已經成爲一個很嚴重的問題了，而這個片子（良宵），它就是在研究這個問題下產生的，在本片的開塲，膠片上面，標着這麽幾句字幕，是：（柏村裏面三樣多，柏樹多，牌坊多，寡婦多……）雖然是很簡單的幾個字，但，它已經把中國數千年來牢不可破的舊習慣，很充分的表現出來，而本片的主旨，出就給它一語道破了。

這個片子的中心意識，無疑的，它是極力抨擊旌我節烈虚僞·片中的主人翁，她本是一個渴望着愛的安慰的靑年女子，不幸丈夫死去，呌她獨守空幃·虚在這種情形之下，牠倒底不是一個活死人，决不能忘却情慾的本能，但是因爲懾於禮敎的威力，又不敢不强自遏制·當她在郊外和情人默默相對時，爲了情慾的衝動，幾及於亂，但那貞節牌坊的幻影，在她的腦中，頓時一個一個的擁現着，她祇有號哭，奔逃了。

除此之外，它還寫着：族長和有夫之婦秘密通姦，口頭上却是一味假仁假義；小土豪詐財凌弱，他爲了不能滿足自己的性慾，倒來干涉嫠婦的自由；老節母壓死在貞節牌坊下，祇落得給人家咒駡她是自作自受·這些這些，它把窮鄕僻野中的怪現象暴露出來，眞可以說是淋漓盡緻致了。

觀（良宵）後 325

— 林辰

在中國世紀式的封建社會裏，貞烈是被視爲至高無上的女性美德的。一座座剝落的巍峨的貞節牌坊下，埋了無數靑春寡婦的𤍠血和靈魂。

（良宵）的全部意識，是　可取的。它用一個靑春寡婦的心靈衝動，與舊觀念的難以解决的鬥爭爲襯托，不但諷剌假道學的僞君子，並且大胆地暴露了舊禮敎的荒謬，殘忍。當這靑春寡婦雲琳被衆手所指斥而用雪去打她，演到雲琳的婆婆毫無顧忌地反駁這些族長族人都是依勢欺凌孱弱的寡婦的時候，這個高潮是很成功的，很有力的引起觀衆們的憤懣和同情。所以（良宵）的意識很適合現在過渡時期的女性，尤其是一班女學生。

演出方面，大槪缺乏穿揷，所以全是靜的調子，但回想寡婦的心理描寫時，却津津然覺其價値。

故事方面，似乎有不很眞實之處。照中國舊式風俗習慣看來，很少責罰不貞的男子的，因爲根本没有判斷男子不貞的習慣。（良宵）中竟有驅逐二十四代孫的事，不知竟有此事否？

技巧一方面我很滿意，雲琳借井水照着自己的容顏，聞琴聲而動脚，都有次序地表現出靑春寡婦的情感。雲琳晒衣時牌坊在她心中動着，她在受（最後審判）時被衆人指斥着，雪中足跡（模倣伏虎美人），族長憤怒的面部特寫（模倣生路），幽會時兩個面影，雲琳躱在樹後送行等等，都有空前的優美的成功。以桃樹作背景，更有哀艷之意。

演員談瑛最好，她的動作表情都以遲慢的西洋派爲長。惟缺乏眼部表情。蔣君超不很有進步，他的表情不很適合劇中的多情的靑年盡家。湯天繡久不見面，而作風一變，大槪有些生硬。飾阿培哥的陳斌遇火一些。其餘平平。

評（良宵） 326

— 古月

講到（良宵）的演出方面，多方都能得到圓滿，這片子始終能給我們一些滿足。

雲琳淘米時，爲本片最精采的一幕，她很幽怨地望着井裏的影子，而當吊桶放下的時候，將那幽怨的影子，一片一片地分散開了。攝影旣佳，表情也深刻，誠能描寫出一個抑壓在舊禮敎下的寡婦，對於自己的靑春發生無限的感槪！所以，雲琳是一個很難扮的角色，一方面顧着自己的名節，一方却不能壓住她靑春之火，處在這兩難的情况下，她能處之泰然，無論如何，是成功的一個。

劉節母是舊禮敎的服者，可是，她能有勇氣揭破這黑幕，這是暗示着人類的覺悟。在覺悟時的表情，是有相當的成績。

朱英是一個小學敎師，他反對禮敎，可是終於失敗了！他𤍠誠的心，仍不能醒悟雲琳，最後便映成這個悲劇。

攝影有兩幕是極好的，尤甚在雲琳磨米和照井的時候。攝柏村的柏樹和牌坊，也有相當的成功。

導演的技術很高，他能使全劇的分配，得着一些很適當的人材。可是，頭兩幕博叙到劉節母的時候，未免太大兜圈子了。

全劇的演出都能得到圓滿，這是最後該說的一句話。同時比（風）是好得多，因爲（風）祇是描寫一個被都市生活的女性，而（良宵）却是描寫整個不幸的女性。

兩天内的驚人消息 327

— 甡芬

聯華吳村加入明星已成事實，現在消息傳來，高占非已加入明星，合同已簽定，月薪五百元，酬勞在外，另外尙有一附帶條件，卽名次除胡蝶以外，不在其他演員之下。

聞蔡楚生也在動搖之中，亦有加入明星之說。

戲劇家左明前與鮑志超合資創辦的太華公司，現因某種關係，公司目下尙難實現，而左明刻由某君的介紹進天一，任編劇及演員的職務。

天一在香港設分公司，邵醉翁特遣其弟邵邨人赴港辦公，聞邨人已與分公司的同人商洽完妥，日内就要返申了。

天一（紅樓春深），（春宵曲）再拍完兩塲大佈景後，卽宣吿完竣。

陳玉梅將俟其主演的（紅樓春深）拍完後，卽繼續主演由張恨水小說改編于思編劇的（美人恩）導演已定由裘　香導演。

明星公司已派人赴杭州拍取時輪金剛法會的新聞片。

天一文書主任高天棲君，昨日連夜編好（紅樓春深）中的（採蓮歌）後，於今晨返原籍紹興省親。

電影小說

奇異酒店（ＷｏｎｄｅｒＢａｒ）五 328

— 叔明

殷納絲和哈雷登了塲，殷納還是在跳舞的時候，和哈雷纠緾不淸。哈雷則表示厭惡，時時加以怒叱，並且屢次三番，故意用力很命地將她摔在地上。並且駡着牠道：（别這樣有氣無力的。你所做的事，自己小心些）。殷納絲被他一推，摔了一交。她抬起頭來對着哈雷喊道：（哈雷！）哈雷道：（你還要那種樣子嗎？）殷納絲道：（你，你不能離開我。我不讓你走。）哈雷道：（你再不停嘴！）他說着故意放出一個很難的步伐，將殷納絲很命地再摔出去。殷納絲又重重地摔了一交。全塲看客雖然知道這都是表演中的部份，但是大家看了那種逼眞的神情，都不禁嚇得氣都透不過來。後來殷納絲說道：（你要帶着雷那德夫人一同走嗎？）哈雷叱道：（我帶她走，關你什麽事？）殷納絲道：（我不准你帶她走！）哈雷發火道：（好！你敢阻擋我的事！）他說着又很命地將她一推，她就倒在地下了。全塲這時都譁然站了起來。亞爾連忙出來打譁着說道：（衆位安心坐下。這是夜夜如此的。）殷納絲慢慢地抬起頭來，縷的鮮血，已經從她的口裏直流出來。她偷偷兒從她的襪帶裏抽出那把剌刀來，隨着音樂的節奏，霍然地站了起來，向着哈雷迎上去。等到走了身，她說：（你不能帶她去！）她將那刀在哈雷的胸膊扎下去。同時音樂鏘然一聲，　然而止。亞爾明白了怎麽回事。哈雷還抱着殷納絲在懷裏。可是他自己也站不住了。四面掌聲雷動。亞爾直奔上去。假裝着慶賀他們，他將兩臂，一邊一個，將哈雷和殷納支撑上起來。哈雷癱軟了，勉强向全塲鞠躬。全塲又大家歡呼起來。亞爾趁着鬧轟轟的當口，扶着他們進去了。

哈雷和殷納絲進了化妝室，殷納絲立卽就暈過去了。等到亞爾再看哈雷的時候，他已經死了。亞爾情急智生，立卽奔出去尋李却。他呌李却帮他的忙，要拿哈雷屍體搬出去，不等殷納絲醒過來。不過舞塲四週都是警察，怎麽混得出去？於是他們預先拿一瓶酒，送給了一個小門外的警察。那個警察有了酒就什麽都不管了。亞爾和李却兩個人，一邊一個，將哈雷的屍體架了起來，祇當他喝醉了，架了出去。他們將哈雷的身體，一架架到那個弗林一尉的車子裏，向他車子的後廂一塞。一回兒弗林上尉來了，他亦不知道車廂裏面有死人，他就跨上了車，開着就走了。臨走他還對着亞爾道：（再會，再會。明天不要忘記了買報看。）亞爾和他擺着手道：（再會吧，上尉。報紙？不忘記，不忘記。你所知道的，還不到一半哩。）他說着就忽忽地進了舞塲。他亦來不及去看殷納絲，就跑到自己化妝室裏，妝扮黑人去表演黑人入天堂的歌舞去了。（未完）

1934.05.22

Attendance of Over a Hundred Representatives from Various Provinces and Cities, Chairman Kong Xiangxi Delivers Opening Remarks, First General Assembly Elects Review Committees for Each Group, 61 Proposals Divided into Four Groups for Review, Representatives of Boat People from Twelve圩 Kneel and Petition Minister Kong 1

(Nanjing) The National Finance Conference held its opening ceremony at the Ministry of Finance Conference Hall on the 21st. After paying respects at the mausoleum at 9 a.m., all the representatives went by car directly to the National Government to attend the National Government Commemoration Week. They returned to the Ministry of Finance at 11 a.m. to hold the opening ceremony. 114 representatives attended. The master of ceremonies, Luo Shuxun, conducted the rituals as prescribed. First, Chairman Kong Xiangxi delivered the opening address, followed by an address from Central Representative Wang Zhaoming, President of the Executive Yuan, an address from National Government Representative Deng Jiayan, and a speech by Zhang Shouyong. Finally, the chairman gave a response and encouraged all the attending representatives. The ceremony concluded at 12:30 p.m., and a photograph was taken before dispersing. (Special dispatch from the 21st)

All Members Pay Respects at the Mausoleum 2

(Nanjing) The National Finance Conference opened on the morning of the 21st. First, Kong Xiangxi, accompanied by over a hundred representatives from various provinces and cities, and heads of finance departments and bureaus, traveled in dozens of cars to pay respects at the mausoleum outside Zhongshan Gate. Kong presided over the ceremony, read the memorial address, and presented a wreath. Kong led the respects at the mausoleum and a photograph was taken in front of the mausoleum before returning to the city together to attend the Commemoration Week at the National Government. After 11 a.m., they returned to the Ministry of Finance to hold the opening ceremony. President Wang, Kong Xiangxi, and Deng Jiayan all delivered addresses. The memorial address for paying respects at the mausoleum read: "On the 21st day of May, in the 23rd year of the Republic of China, Kong Xiangxi, Executive Member of the Central Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, Vice President of the Executive Yuan, and Minister of Finance, respectfully accompanies all members of the Second National Finance Conference to pay respects at the tomb of the Premier and to report to him in writing: Since the 20th year of our nation, chaos and turmoil have continued, and soldiers and bandits have run rampant, leading to the devastation of rural villages, the decline of all industries, the inadequacy of national expenditures, and the stagnation of people's livelihoods. Recently, we have suffered externally from the tide of the global economic panic and internally from extremely serious national disasters. We are acutely aware that without enriching wealth, it is impossible to alleviate poverty, and without enriching the people, it is impossible to support the fallen. Xiangxi, with his limited abilities, shoulders the heavy responsibility of managing finances. He is deeply concerned that plans may be incomplete and measures may be insufficient. Therefore, he convened this conference to gather collective wisdom, hoping to achieve concerted efforts and to achieve the effect of relieving difficulties and rescuing dangers. At the beginning of the conference, we offer our utmost sincerity to inform our Premier. May our Premier, mindful of the difficulties and dangers, bless our people. May his spirit in heaven truly witness this. We report." (Central News Agency dispatch from the 21st)

Minister Kong Delivers Opening Address 3

(Nanjing) Today, this ministry convened the Second National Finance Conference. We are honored to have President Wang, the representative of the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government, attend and deliver an address. Representatives from various regions, experts, and important financial personnel from various provinces and cities have come from afar to attend the conference, gathering talents in one place to make comprehensive plans. Xiangxi sincerely expresses his honor and welcomes you. In July of the 17th year, this ministry convened the First National Finance Conference. At that time, national unification had not been long achieved, military affairs had just ended, and political tutelage was about to begin. The entire nation was eager for governance. At that time, the work focused on the reorganization of finances, hoping to gradually implement the resolutions, progressing from reorganization to construction. Unexpectedly, in the six years since then, natural disasters and man-made calamities have followed one after another, famines have been frequent, and communist bandits have proliferated. In the past three years, the national crisis and the global economic panic have become even more severe, placing the country and society in a precarious situation. Fortunately, the reorganization work, relying on the efforts of colleagues, although without significant achievements, has had a course to follow. However, the social economy is declining day by day, and farmers suffer from low grain prices and heavy taxes. The income from hard work is insufficient to make a living. Industry and commerce are declining due to the angry tide of the economic downturn, and imports increase year by year. In the past, the problem was financial disorder, but now it is compounded by depletion. Disorder still needs reorganization, and depletion needs relief. Both need to be addressed concurrently.

Finance is the lifeline of the nation, just like blood to the human body. It must circulate entirely to have a healthy physique. If each section acts independently, it will inevitably lead to imbalance and even paralysis. Today, when we talk about relief, there is no way to preserve the dying vitality without making every effort to cultivate the people's strength. To revive the countryside and revitalize the market, we must first enable the people to live and work in peace. The military authorities are now devoting all their efforts to suppressing the communist bandits. In terms of finance, it is urgent to eliminate the burdens of the people so that the suffering they directly endure can be gradually relieved. At the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Committee in January of this year, Xiangxi proposed the reorganization of the land tax and the reduction of surcharges. The General Assembly resolved to pass it, and the Central Political Conference sent it to the Executive Yuan for execution by the Ministry of Finance. However, this matter is significant and requires the strength of the masses to facilitate progress, and it especially depends on the local authorities to discuss implementation plans based on local conditions. There are myriad aspects to financial management, which cannot be accomplished by one person alone. At this time of declining people's livelihoods and national crisis, there are many priorities in planning restoration, and the order of urgency must be carefully considered. Moreover, in today's China, there are many things to discuss in reorganizing finances, and the following issues deserve special attention:

(1) How should we find alternative ways to compensate for reducing land tax surcharges so as to alleviate the people's difficulties without hindering construction?

(2) What kind of good taxes should be established to replace the abolition of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies and to find new sources of revenue?

(3) How should the tax system be improved to ensure that the people's burden is fair and does not lead to uneven or excessive burdens?

(4) How should the foundation of local budgets be determined to ensure that revenue and expenditure are balanced?

(5) How should national revenue and expenditure be coordinated to balance surpluses and deficits and avoid uneven distribution of hardship and prosperity among different regions?

(6) How should the ratio between administrative expenses and business expenses be properly determined to ensure that funds are not wasted and that no task is neglected?

(7) How should the qualifications, guarantees, and reward and punishment methods of tax officials be determined to increase tax revenue?

(8) How should the currency system be reorganized to facilitate the people and stabilize the market?

(9) How should finance be circulated and idle funds be utilized to support production enterprises?

(10) China's foundation is agriculture. The rural economy is now on the verge of bankruptcy. How should we find ways to provide relief to assist farmers in increasing production and to seek the revival of agriculture and the development of abundant resources?

(11) Industry and commerce are declining day by day. How should we find ways to encourage domestic goods and support production to reduce leakage and seek economic development?

(12) Regarding local security, transportation, education, and other policies, how should we utilize the capabilities of autonomy and self-defense to reduce expenditure and the burden of tax surcharges?

(13) How should the New Life Movement be promoted to advocate thrift and foster integrity?

(14) How should the central and local governments support each other internally and externally to jointly seek development?

The above are just a few of the major issues that need to be resolved urgently. The reorganization of the land tax, the equalization of burdens, the determination of local budgets, the opening of tax sources, and the reform of the currency system are particularly urgent. They require collective wisdom and careful planning. Over the years, rental taxes have increased, and in various cities and provinces, new policies have been implemented for important purposes. The central government is well aware of the unavoidable difficulties. However, considering the people's strength, it is truly unbearable. Resolving to eliminate them is like a hero cutting off his wrist. Although reducing surcharges to relieve the people's difficulties will harm local income, thoroughly reorganizing tax revenue, developing production, and cultivating tax sources can increase revenue and may be sufficient to offset the losses. The central and local governments are originally one body, sharing weal and woe, and there are originally no boundaries to divide. In this time of crisis, it is especially important to unite sincerely to overcome difficulties. Therefore, although the central government's finances have been extremely difficult in recent years, if there is an urgent need for local governments, it will still make every effort to provide assistance even when there seems to be no way to do so. For example, recently, as the communist areas in Jiangxi Province have gradually recovered, the countryside urgently needs revival. Therefore, Chairman Chiang and Chairman Xiong discussed with President Wang and Xiangxi and decided to exempt the entire province from exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies. The insufficient funds will be supplemented by the ministry. However, this is only a temporary measure and not a fundamental solution. To seek a fundamental solution, we must open up sources of production and reduce wasteful spending. The key lies in determining the budget. The central government must have a thorough understanding of the actual revenue and expenditure of local governments in order to make appropriate allocations and have sufficient measures. This is what the central and local governments should encourage each other to do.

There are three reasons why our country's finances have been weak and why accumulated malpractices have been difficult to reform. First, corrupt officials engage in private gain and abuse their power to enrich themselves. Second, construction is not carefully considered in terms of urgency, and spending is not frugal. Third, officials are extravagant by nature and waste public funds excessively. Therefore, what the country takes from the people is not small, but through repeated exploitation, little wealth remains. The country is poor and the people are poor, and this is the root cause. The officials in charge of tax collection have known the source of these malpractices for a long time, but they have tolerated them in silence, mostly out of multiple considerations and bending over backwards to protect them. To fully express the bottom line would be inconvenient for private gain. It must be known that when the government is in a time of crisis, the way to save the situation lies in bringing the national finances into order. If the finances are not in order, there is no way to carry out governance. If governance cannot be carried out, how can the country be revived? Revolution must first revolutionize the heart. Public officials must thoroughly remove accumulated bad habits and completely eliminate old stains before they can talk about promoting benefits and eliminating malpractices, and being clean and serving the public. Otherwise, even if the discussions result in concrete plans, they will not be implemented, or they will not be implemented effectively, and they will remain empty words. This is what is hoped for from all public officials in the country to have a deep awareness of.

The national crisis is now serious, and the global economic downturn has spread to our country. Countries are too busy saving themselves from the economic panic to help others. Our country's production is backward and its economy is declining. If we do not quickly seek a way to save the situation, we will be heading towards danger. The most important thing at present is for the government and the people to work together. The people must strictly supervise the collecting officials to prevent them from engaging in corruption and enriching themselves. They must also deeply understand their tax obligations and work hard to produce to enrich tax sources. If the top and bottom are of one mind and work together to save the situation, the national economy and the people's livelihood can be enriched, and the crises of the future can be averted. This is what is hoped for from the people to have a deep understanding of.

In short, the convocation of this National Finance Conference is not only to discuss the reorganization of finances but also to address the prosperity and decline of the people's livelihood and the well-being of the nation, which are closely related. I deeply hope that you will remember the difficulties that the Premier faced in creating the Republic of China and the hard-earned legacy left by our Yellow Emperor ancestors. The current dangerous situation and the responsibility that lies on our shoulders are extremely heavy and great. We must have the spirit of self-denial and sacrifice and a deep and clear understanding. Officials and people, internal and external, must work together as one to reverse this precarious situation. Finance is the lifeline of the nation, and the blood must circulate, as has been said before. A person who suffers from anemia or toxic blood will be weak and sick. Today, our country is suffering from this disease. You have come here specifically to work for the country's blood purification and blood transfusion. However, without thoroughly removing the selfish heart for oneself, the country will still be unsavable. This conference, although for the purpose of saving finances, is actually for the purpose of saving the country and saving the people. In other words, it can be said to be a salvation conference. All experts, representatives from various provinces and cities, and financial personnel from various provinces and cities must deeply understand that in this time of extraordinary national crisis, they should painfully remember the meaning of loving the country and forgetting the family, and being selfless and forgetting the self. They should jointly discuss how to overcome difficulties, not engage in high-sounding and impractical words, and not engage in empty and unrealistic theories. The words should all have substance and be feasible to implement, so that they can achieve the effect of relieving difficulties and supporting the crisis through a step-by-step approach. This is what Xiangxi hopes for. We look forward to your wise advice and await your excellent remarks.

Photography of the Opening Ceremony of the Finance Conference 4

President Wang Delivers Address 5

(Nanjing) President Wang said in his address at the Finance Conference: "The convening of today's Finance Conference is of great significance, and it is even more significant to convene it during this time of national crisis. Those responsible for finances now feel a contradictory pain. On the one hand, they must raise funds from the people, and on the other hand, the people no longer have the ability to pay. It is difficult to find a solution to this contradiction. China has been an agricultural country since ancient times. All that the government needs to do is to achieve the eight characters of 'simple government, clear laws, light taxes, and low levies.' The amount taken from the people should be small, and the amount of work done for the people does not need to be much. Since the opening of China to foreign countries, the situation has changed greatly. The agriculture, industry, and commerce of various countries have been highly developed, and competition is fierce. China is in this international environment, and what is taken from the people and used for the people is not comparable to before. Just look at the military. Building a gunboat requires tens of millions or hundreds of millions of military expenses. Everything else is the same. For example, in terms of transportation, foreign countries can transport troops to China with extremely fast warships. According to our past experience, it takes 20 to 30 days to transport one or two divisions of troops from Jiangxi to Shanghai. How can we avoid the danger of the relief troops not arriving in time? However, the construction of railways and highways requires huge amounts of money. If we still use the eight characters of 'simple government, clear laws, light taxes, and low levies' as the standard, our country will not be able to exist. I know that those serving in the central and local governments feel that China lacks the conditions needed for a modern country and must try their best to catch up. However, the difficulty of finance and the exhaustion of the economy make it impossible to start. According to the report of the Customs, imports exceeded exports by 600 million last year. The people eat foreign rice and flour, and the people wear foreign cotton and yarn. Almost everything we need in life depends on foreign countries. They have strong capital and can sell at low profits and high volume. We have weak capital. How can we compete? All agriculture, industry, and commerce cannot compete with others. The countryside is already very desolate, and society is already very poor. Now is the time when the people need relief. If we continue to levy taxes and extract the fat of the people, it is really unbearable. Therefore, the central and local governments alike must find money on the one hand and not ask the people for more money on the other hand. This contradictory phenomenon has become the pain of our finances. As for the solution, Vice President Kong has already said a lot, and I cannot say more. However, at this time when the national crisis is most severe and the national economy is on the verge of bankruptcy, the people passively hope for the government's relief and hope for the reorganization of taxes. Actively, the government should do a lot of work in production and construction. This financial problem and tax problem must be solved. If it cannot be solved, there will only be destruction. Therefore, this Finance Conference is not only a financial problem, but also a problem about the life of the nation. I hope that the central and local representatives and experts will, during these few days of meetings, base their knowledge and experience on finding appropriate solutions. This solution is the way out for China's finances and the way out for the Chinese nation." (Special dispatch from the 21st)

Representative of the National Government Delivers Speech 6

(Nanjing) Representative of the National Government, Deng Jiayan, said in his address: "What I want to say now is what Mencius said, 'The loss of the world by Jie and Zhou was the loss of their people, the loss of their hearts. There is a way to gain the world: gain the people, and you will gain the world. There is a way to gain the people: gain their hearts, and you will gain the people. There is a way to gain their hearts: gather what they desire, and do not impose what they hate.' This is truly the best teaching for us. The Premier's Principle of People's Livelihood also focuses on relieving the people's economic oppression. Today, the surcharges on land taxes exceed the regular taxes by more than ten times. In addition, there are exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies. The burden on the people can be imagined. I hope that in this conference, we can seek practical solutions and implement all resolutions conscientiously. 'Governance does not lie in much talk, but in how to implement it.' This is especially what should be contributed to everyone present." (Special dispatch from the 21st)

Zhang Shouyong's Speech 7

(Nanjing) At the opening of the Finance Conference, expert member Zhang Shouyong gave a speech, roughly saying that the national crisis is now severe and the economy is on the verge of bankruptcy. President Wang mentioned that the Customs' imports exceeded exports by 600 million yuan each year. How to overcome this crisis must be carefully studied. China is an agricultural country, but in recent years, the countryside is on the verge of total collapse. This spring, Shouyong returned to his hometown for business and talked with the general farmers. According to the farmers, they are still in debt after paying the rent. China has few large farmers and many small farmers. Because labor costs are high and rice prices are low, and taxes are heavy, this is a major cause of rural bankruptcy. At this Finance Conference, representatives from various provinces and cities and experts gathered together to discuss and will surely be able to come up with remedial measures for China's finances in the future. At the same time, we must also fight for a breath in the international arena. Shouyong, as a citizen, hopes that the central and local gentlemen will make a firm decision. At a minimum, from today onwards, never increase taxes. As for the previous excessive surcharges, there should be a gradual reduction method, and it is hoped that exorbitant and petty taxes will be abolished immediately, and so on. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 21st)

The newly arrived representatives included Yan Yangchu (expert member), Sheng Shengyi (Director of the Jiangsu Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Tax Bureau), Lu Yansun (Fujian Salt Commissioner), Xu Fu (Fujian Province Representative and Director of the Fujian Finance Department), Zeng Rongpu (Secretary-General of the Financial Reorganization Committee), Cai Zengji (Shanghai City Representative and Director of the Shanghai Finance Bureau), Tang Wenxuan (Representative of the Rural Reconstruction Committee), Chen Xizhang (External Representative), Chen Changheng (Expert Committee Member), Xu Shilian (Economic Council Representative), Wang Zhixin (Rural Reconstruction Council Representative), Wu Song　 (External Representative), Guo Xinshong (Ministry of Communications Representative), Wu Chengying (Director of the Zhejiang Finance Department), Sun Shengwu (Expert Member), Yan Lu (Ministry of Justice Representative), etc.

First General Assembly 9

(Nanjing) The Finance Conference held its first meeting at 2 p.m. on the 21st. 119 members attended. Kong Xiangxi was the chairman, Zou Lin was the vice chairman, and Qin Fen was the secretary-general. After the meeting opened, Kong reported that 61 proposals had been received. To save time, proposals with similar agendas should be divided into four groups for review. The first group will review matters related to the reorganization of land tax surcharges in various provinces. The second group will review matters related to the reorganization of old taxes, the abolition of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies, and the improvement of local tax systems. The third group will review the determination of local budgets. The fourth group will review proposals that do not belong to the above groups. After Kong finished his report, Qin read the reasons for the proposals and the list of review committee members designated by the chairman. Proposal 1 regarding the reorganization of local finances (submitted by the minister for discussion) was assigned to the first group. Proposals 2 to 16 were assigned to the first group for review. Proposals 17 to 30 were assigned to the second group for review. Proposals 31 to 40 were assigned to the third group for review. Proposals 41 to 56 were assigned to the fourth group for review. Proposal 57 was assigned to the second group. Proposal 58 was assigned to the fourth group. Proposals 59 and 60 were assigned to the first group. The chairman of the first group committee was Peng Xuepei, and the members were Mao Longzhang, Zhang Miao, Zheng Zhenyu, Xu Fu, Zhu Jingzhou, Yang Mianzhong, Wu Jiantao, etc., totaling 28 people. The chairman of the second group committee was Zhang Shouyong, and the members were Jia Shiyi, Zhou Xiuwen, Liu Kuidu, Hong Huaiyou, Zou Fang, etc., totaling 25 people. The chairman of the third group committee was Ma Yinchu, and the members were Yang Rumei, Zhao Dihua, Wang Xiangrong, Pang Songzhou, Li Yingsheng, etc., totaling 24 people. Finally, it was decided that temporary motions would be submitted to the General Assembly for discussion by this Wednesday. The meeting adjourned at 4 p.m. In the evening, Kong held a banquet at the Lizi Society to welcome all members. President Wang also scheduled a banquet for the members of the conference at the Overseas Chinese Reception Center on the 22nd and invited ministers to accompany him. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 21st)

Current Affairs Commentary

The Disarmament Conference on the Verge of Collapse 10

— Heng

Although there is still talk that the Disarmament Conference Committee in Geneva will meet on the 29th of this month, its hope of success has been exhausted. One reason is that Germany's recently announced military budget has exceeded the limits allowed by the Treaty of Versailles.

The country also feels that the Disarmament Conference is about to fail, so it is eager to strengthen its national defense. From these three aspects, it can be seen that the fate of the Disarmament Conference is hanging by a thread, and the pronouncement of its death sentence is only a matter of time.

For now, leaving aside this fragmented phenomenon and focusing on the root cause, the reason why disarmament cannot be achieved is even more obvious. International peace must be based on friendship, and the attainment of friendship must be based on fairness. Otherwise, it will be difficult to avoid the repeated breeding of old hatreds and new grudges, and the beautiful name of peace will become a mere bubble. Perhaps some fail to observe the inversion of cause and effect, thinking that if disarmament is achieved, peace can be guaranteed. They do not know that without the elements and conditions of peace, advocating disarmament is either foolish or deceitful. Therefore, seeking peace through disarmament is a direct example of abandoning the root and pursuing the branch. The reason why disarmament is unsuccessful is not that the countries lack sincerity.

When the European War was in progress, the Allied countries called it the "war to end war," meaning that there would be no more suffering from war after this, once and for all. After the war stopped, they should not have imposed the shackles of the Treaty of Versailles on Germany. After the treaty was signed, they should not have ignored the clear wording of universal disarmament in the treaty, making Germany suffer alone. Unexpectedly, the Allied countries had not yet completed their victory song when their old habits reemerged. Secret treaties to divide the future spoils of war emerged one after another, such as dividing the land of the defeated countries, extorting reparations from the defeated countries, and restricting the armaments of the defeated countries. They used every means to the extreme. How could they gain the goodwill of the defeated countries? Therefore, the day the Treaty of Versailles was signed was also the time when the next great war was sown.

Furthermore, disarmament and the League of Nations were originally inseparable. The success of disarmament would naturally increase the prestige of the League of Nations. However, there must first be a strong and powerful League of Nations before it can use its prestige to promote the success of disarmament. Since the September 18th Incident, the weakness and incompetence of the League of Nations have been fully exposed. The reason why Japan dared to brazenly withdraw from the League of Nations and the reason why Germany dared to follow in Japan's footsteps were all the results of seeing through this weakness. Even saying that the omen of the failure of disarmament today can be seen again at the beginning of Japan's invasion of our Northeast is not an overstatement.

As for the direct cause, it is the rise of Hitler in Germany. In December 1932, the five countries of Britain, the United States, France, Germany, and Italy signed the so-called protocol recognizing the principle of equal status for German armaments. The new British draft on March 16 of the following year allowed Germany to establish an army of 200,000 men within eight years. France's attitude also seemed to have room for maneuver. However, after Hitler came to power and vigorously implemented his active foreign policy, he deeply incurred the jealousy of France. Last winter, Germany withdrew from the League of Nations, and the Disarmament Conference was already in a desperate situation. The reason why it still had a glimmer of hope was that Britain mediated between France and Germany to seek a compromise. Unexpectedly, Germany announced a new budget, openly increasing military spending, causing France to refuse to negotiate further with Germany. The one glimmer of hope for the conference was cut off by Hitler's tough attitude, which is truly regrettable.

The heart denies that Germany has any more rights to equal armaments. France's fear of Germany and its own isolation are also reflected from this. If France were to go to war with Germany today, the assistance it would receive abroad would be far less than in 1914. It can be predicted that Britain will take a neutral attitude as much as possible towards the war between France and Germany, except for maintaining its obligations under the Locarno Treaty. The fact that it wants to conclude an air force agreement with the Paris government shows that its fear of France is not small. As for Italy after the war, its interests have always conflicted with France. Although it cannot be said that it will definitely help Germany attack France in the future, it will inevitably sit on the sidelines and reap the benefits. The only support that France can rely on is the Little Entente. However, Austria-Hungary is manipulated by Italy, and the Little Entente is restrained by Austria-Hungary. How much substance is there in the Little Entente? It is truly questionable. On the other hand, Germany's developed machinery industry, strong national will, and prevalent martial spirit make it not very difficult to prepare for war. Even in terms of population, it far surpasses France. It is said that between 1936 and 1940, the number of French combatants will only be half of what it was at the outbreak of the last great war. This alone is enough to make them feel a great threat.

In short, the Disarmament Conference convened by the League of Nations has reached the stage of death. Afterwards, the situation in Europe will inevitably become more dangerous. No matter which direction British policy tends towards, or whether it maintains neutrality, it can be asserted that its focus is on seeking self-preservation as quickly as possible. The impact of this may be enough to make the British change their understanding of the Far Eastern problem, which is something that we Chinese people should pay close attention to and plan for ourselves.

Major Conference Agenda 11

(A) Reporting Matters (1) The Draft Local Tax Regulations for Financial Revenue and Expenditure System Law, submitted by Legislator Wei Ting-sheng from the Legislative Yuan. (2) Planning documents and reports submitted by various provinces and cities. (3) Various reference tables compiled by this Ministry. (B) Discussion Items (1) Plan for Reorganizing Local Finances (proposed by the Minister). (2) Draft Regulations on Land Reporting (proposed by the Minister). (3) The reorganization of Fujian's land tax should start with the handling of reporting, ensuring that land taxes are consistent, burdens are equal, and that a pilot census be carried out in the first county, gradually expanding to eliminate long-standing abuses and increase tax revenue (proposed by the Fujian Finance Department). (4) Plan for Reorganizing Land Tax (proposed by the Gansu Finance Department). (5) Proposal to determine that the direction of land tax reorganization should emphasize the equal importance of correcting land registration, redefining the tax system, and reforming the collection system (proposed by expert members Xiao, Tang Qiyu, Zhang Miao, and Wan Guoding). (6) National Fundamental Land Reorganization Plan (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (7) Request to issue public bonds for land reorganization and conduct land surveys to implement fundamental solutions for land tax reorganization (proposed by the Jiangxi Finance Department). (8) The increased land tax from land reporting conducted by various provinces should be planned comprehensively, and security fees from each county should be collected and spent uniformly by the province (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (9) Implement measures to reduce additional land taxes to alleviate people's difficulties, in accordance with the Ministry of Finance's supplementary measures for land tax reorganization (proposed by the Fujian Finance Department). (10) Proposal to determine the funding for local agencies in each county based on county level or population size, standardize the additional tax rate for land tax in each county, and uniformly collect taxes to achieve an equal burden (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (11) Land tax in each province should only be divided into provincial regular tax and county surtax, and all other categories should be deleted (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (12) Implement land tax in each province based on land value, and abolish all regular tax surcharges, collecting tax revenue uniformly and distributing it equally between provinces and counties (proposed by the Henan Finance Department). (13) Propose that provinces in prosperous areas first conduct a pilot land value tax to promote the idea (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (14) Implement land value tax to replace land taxes (proposed by Zhunnan Transportation Deputy). (15) Propose that only tax exemptions be offered in years of disaster and crop failure, and not deferred tax payments (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (16) Request that salt production be returned to the people, exempting the collection of grain, to comply with the standards for dividing national and local income (proposed by the Finance Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government). (17) Request that various provinces eliminate miscellaneous taxes to save the cotton industry from crisis (proposed by the National Economic Committee). (18) Request the thorough exemption of business tax on sales of yarn and cloth by yarn factory branches and offices, to maintain the cotton industry and avoid disputes (proposed by the National Economic Committee). (19) Request the abolition of parcel post tax and transit tax (proposed by the Ministry of Transportation). (20) Request that measures be taken to collect business tax from foreign merchants to maintain Chinese business operations and increase revenue (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (21) Propose that the tax rate for deed tax in each province be uniformly reduced to provide relief and increase revenue (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (22) Because the penalties stipulated in the Deed Tax Regulations are excessively high, it is proposed to amend and reduce them to alleviate the people's hardships and maintain the tax base (proposed by the Hebei Provincial Government). (23) Abolish local surcharges under tobacco and alcohol categories (proposed by Wu Qiding, Director of the Tax Administration). (24) Provinces may not re-levy taxes on goods that have already been subject to the central consolidated tax (proposed by Wu Qiding, Director of the Tax Administration). (25) To thoroughly explain the past situation of abolishing arbitrary taxes and levies in Hubei Province, and propose future reform guidelines, please make a public decision (proposed by the Hubei Finance Department). (26) It is proposed that local areas in various provinces should never be allowed to establish categories under salt, collect surcharges, or interfere with national taxes; reiterate clear orders and make them strict cases (proposed by the Henan Salt Sales Bureau). (27) Propose improving the current business tax, merging all miscellaneous taxes, reforming the business tax, and establishing a tax system to promote the sound development of local finances (proposed by expert member Liu Kuida). (28) Propose amending the Business Tax Law (proposed by the Finance Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government). (29) Propose to crack down on the surcharges on salt in Anhui, and request improvements in the collection method to prevent embezzlement (proposed by Tang Shiwan, Director of the Anhui Salt Transport Bureau). (30) The tax levied on cotton dealers in Tianjin is a disguised restoration of likin; please investigate and determine the matter, and crack down on it according to law to maintain national credibility and alleviate merchants' hardships (proposed by the National Economic Committee). (31) Re-divide the standards for national and local revenue and expenditure (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (32) Propose that all judicial expenses be paid by the national treasury (proposed by the Finance Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government). (33) Request that the portion of Gansu Province's national revenue and expenditure be directly managed and paid by the central government (proposed by the Gansu Finance Department). (34) Propose to divide the tax scope of provinces and counties, unify the collection agencies of each province and county, and separately reduce or abolish miscellaneous taxes (proposed by expert member Tang Qiyu). (35) To thoroughly explain the past situation of determining county local budgets in Hubei Province, and propose improvement measures, please make a public decision (proposed by the Hubei Finance Department). (36) Local finances in each province should strictly implement unified collection and expenditure (proposed by the Henan Finance Department). (37) Determine local budget methods (proposed by the National Government Accounting Office). (38) Set a deadline for the establishment of local budgets and strictly implement spending within income, so that revenue and expenditure are appropriate (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (39) Propose to prohibit counties from levying extra donations after the budget is announced to alleviate the people's burden (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (40) For provinces with less revenue, after reducing additional land taxes and abolishing arbitrary taxes and levies, necessary expenditures should be subsidized by the central government to maintain provincial operations (proposed by the Anhui Finance Department). (41) Request the establishment of a land bank to enrich rural capital, and adopt a protective tariff policy for foreign agricultural products (proposed by expert member Xiang Naiqi). (42) Central and local finances should be mutually supportive to achieve balanced development (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (43) Anhui Province's special construction expenses for the 23rd year of the Republic are severely insufficient and cannot be raised; please request the central government to allocate special funds on a monthly basis to facilitate local construction (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (44) Provincial universities in each province should be converted into national universities, or subsidized by the central government to improve them (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (45) Implement inheritance tax, increase taxes on tobacco, alcohol, and cigarettes, and use this revenue to open banks in various provinces and larger counties and towns, allowing loans to farmers and workers to benefit people's livelihoods and cultivate the nation's strength (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (46) Determine border defense funding, improve the financial system of Xikang, to strengthen national defense and eliminate long-standing abuses (proposed by Ma Ze Zhao, representative of the people of Xikang stationed in Beijing). (47) Request that measures be taken to gradually revise commercial treaties with countries such as Britain and the United States to improve the national economy and save it from crisis (proposed by Cai Guanghui, Counselor of the Ministry of Finance). (48) Crack down on provinces and cities that set up local banks without authorization (proposed by Cai Guanghui, Counselor of the Ministry of Finance). (49) Propose to include Gansu's local tobacco in a provincial special tax area to provide relief (proposed by the Gansu Finance Department). (50) Propose to reduce the autonomous expenses of each county to reduce the people's burden (proposed by the Shandong Finance Department). (51) Propose that the central government allocate funds to develop Guizhou's coal and iron resources to open up sources of profit and close loopholes (proposed by the Guizhou Finance Department). (52) Anhui Province's rice sales are mainly to Guangdong and Chaozhou; please request the central government to issue a general order to Guangdong and Fujian to uniformly collect import taxes on foreign rice according to the standard, to resist the dumping of foreign rice and maintain Anhui's rice market (proposed by the Finance Department of the Anhui Provincial Government). (53) Establish county finance bureaus to implement unified collection and expenditure, to determine county local budgets, and propose to abolish arbitrary taxes and levies (proposed by the Fujian Finance Department). (54) Propose to abolish all kinds of miscellaneous taxes currently in effect in Gansu, and request that the central government allocate funds to provide assistance and compensation (proposed by the Gansu Finance Department). (55) Request the implementation of inheritance tax in accordance with the draft regulations and implementing rules established at the National Finance Conference in the 17th year of the Republic, to benefit finances as soon as possible (proposed by the Shandong Provincial Government). (56) Regarding the proposal to find ways to restore the Zhangjiakou-Kubu transportation (proposed by the Chahar Finance Department). (57) Immediately abolish harsh and petty taxes (proposed by expert member Zhang Shouyong). (58) Establish national banks in each county (proposed by expert member Zhang Shouyong). (59) Reorganize land and restrict fees (proposed by expert member Zhang Shouyong). (60) Gradually reduce additional land taxes over the years (proposed by expert member Zhang Shouyong).

Petition from Representatives of Boatmen of Twelve Weirs 12

(Nanjing) This morning, they went to the financial conference to petition for maintaining sailing transportation. Several people first met with Ma Taiqi, Director of the Salt Affairs Department. Ma promised to forward their intentions. In the afternoon, they met with Minister Kong, who promised to find ways to maintain all points of the request and said that he was drafting short-term and long-term solutions. The representatives reported Kong's replies to the entire group of boatmen representatives. Some believed that since the short-term and long-term solutions had not been formally announced, they could not consider it satisfactory. They were unwilling to return to the weir before the government gave a satisfactory reply and scheduled to go to the central government to petition on the 22nd (Special Dispatch on the 21st).

(Nanjing) Xu Haishen and over three hundred representatives of the sailors of eighteen gangs of salt-transporting sailing ships from Twelve Weirs went to the Ministry of Finance during a conference held at the Ministry on the morning of the 21st to petition for changing back to sail and abolishing motorized transport. Ma Dai was first sent by the Ministry of Finance to meet them and promised to convey their intentions. At one o'clock in the afternoon, Minister Kong personally met them. The representatives knelt on the ground and cried bitterly. Kong then instructed the Salt Administration to summon transport merchants to quickly devise relief measures (Central Dispatch on the 21st).

A Glimpse of Proposals 13

(Topic) Please exempt various provinces from miscellaneous taxes to save the cotton industry from crisis. (Reason) Regarding the matter of the proposal, after the implementation of consolidated taxes in the cotton industry, the tax rate it bears is several times higher than the old tax. The original expectation was "one item, one tax," which would be implemented nationwide, no longer subject to exploitation similar to likin. However, as the law has been in effect for a long time, various provinces have new taxes emerging endlessly. For example, Hunan has production and sales taxes and road construction donations; Jiangxi has production and sales taxes; Hubei has brokerage taxes, etc. All of these are within the consolidated tax area. Those not within the consolidated tax area include Sichuan with landing taxes, import donations, and bandit suppression donations; Guangdong has the heavy re-levy of consolidated tax; and other miscellaneous taxes similar to likin are numerous, and the burden is particularly heavy. What is even more serious is that in Shandong Province along the Jiaoji Railway line, only Chinese yarn shops have the burden of business tax, while Japanese merchants do not have this tax, resulting in Chinese yarn sales being completely occupied by Japanese yarn. Although this committee has repeatedly appealed to the central government, it has not been thoroughly resolved. Therefore, this case is specially submitted, requesting the fundamental elimination of all miscellaneous taxes on yarn, cotton, and cloth in various provinces to relieve the cotton industry.

(Topic) Please thoroughly exempt yarn factory branches and offices from business tax on sales of yarn and cloth to maintain the cotton industry and avoid disputes. (Reason) Article 1 of the Business Tax Law states, "Factories that have already paid factory tax to the central government are exempt from business tax." Article 5 of the Cotton Yarn Consolidated Tax Regulations states, "Cotton yarn that has already paid consolidated tax and its directly woven products shall not be subject to other taxes and levies when transported and sold in various provinces." According to the Business Tax Law, factories that have already paid factory tax to the central government are exempt from business tax. Therefore, branches and factories are one entity, representing the head factory, and should naturally also be exempt. According to the Consolidated Tax Regulations, cotton yarn and its woven products shall not be subject to other taxes and levies when transported and sold in various provinces after consolidated tax has already been paid. Therefore, the scope of the consolidated tax is extremely broad and does not only refer to production tax. Since it is called "transport and sale," there are naturally business activities. Since it is said that "other taxes and levies shall not be levied," business tax should naturally not be levied. It was found that on April 28th of this year, the Ministry of Finance communicated to various provinces and cities the nature of the exemption from business tax for branch offices established by factories or companies that have paid consolidated tax for further clarification as follows: "For branch offices established in various places by factories or companies that have paid consolidated tax, if their business is only to deliver goods and collect payments on behalf of the head factory or head company, and they themselves have no capital or net profit income, and do not concurrently operate other businesses, and are indeed the main body of the head factory or head company, they are exempt from business tax." Although the explanation is already clear, the financial departments of various provinces still do not understand the word "delivery," believing that the head factory's goods can only be delivered to merchants by the branch office and cannot be sold to merchants. Therefore, disputes have not been completely avoided. However, the official letter from the Ministry of Finance replying to this committee stated that "For various manufacturers who set up branch offices in various places, if they are only for promotion and contact, the request for exemption from business tax is still feasible." However, when communicating to various provinces and cities, it said "deliver goods and collect payments" instead of "sell goods and collect payments." Therefore, the so-called "eliminating difficulties for collection agencies and resolving disputes for manufacturers" has not been thoroughly implemented. At a time when the cotton industry is extremely depressed, the suffering of manufacturers should be thoroughly resolved, changing "delivery" to "sale" to avoid disputes. (The above proposal is from the National Economic Committee)

(Topic) Determine local budget methods. (Methods) 1. Prepare and submit budgets on time: Detailed regulations are provided in the budget charter and budget law. The legislative purpose is to determine revenue and expenditure and limit additional funding. If provincial and municipal governments can prepare budgets on time in the future, financial difficulties can be gradually resolved. 2. Prepare realistic budgets, with the principle of matching revenue and expenditure. However, the budgets prepared by various provinces and cities either have more expenditure than revenue or more revenue than expenditure, which is inconsistent with the principle of matching. If balance is forced by using fictitious revenue and expenditure to embellish the situation temporarily, it is not allowed according to the correct purpose of the budget. 3. Strive for self-sufficiency. It is generally recognized nationwide that the central government is currently facing financial difficulties and is unable to subsidize local areas. After the abolition of likin in various provinces and cities, the central government allocated funds to subsidize them, which was originally a temporary expedient. If local areas do not have a plan for self-sufficiency, and face incidents where the central government is unable to take care of them and the source of funds suddenly dries up, the danger is worrying. It seems that without the determination of self-sufficiency, it is not enough to consolidate the foundation of local finances. 4. Spend within income. The promotion of government affairs depends entirely on the amount of funds, and the amount of funds depends on the priority of importance and urgency. The financial reorganization methods of various provinces and cities vary, but the basic principle at present is to spend within income. According to the investigation, Chairman Chiang reorganized the local finances of the bandit suppression areas in Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces, comprehensively managed and allocated the budgets of the three provinces for the 21st and 22nd years of the Republic, and greatly reduced them. What the provincial authorities previously considered to be insufficient to cover expenses and impossible to cope with is now roughly appropriate. This is based on the principle of spending within income, and then determining the policy direction to avoid the situation of supply and demand not meeting, sighing to the roof, or causing annoyance to the people and exhausting the tax base. The above four items are the methods to resolve current difficulties. As for the fundamental plan for determining the budget, the following two points should also be noted: 1. Save on administrative expenses to expand business expenses. In March of the 20th year of the Republic, the Executive Yuan, according to the report of the Ministry of Interior, stipulated that the administrative expenses of each province should not exceed three-fifths of the business expenses. Business expenses are related to local construction, culture, and economy. To improve from this, the provincial and municipal governments should be responsible for reducing administrative expenses, leaving room for construction needs. 2. Opening up financial resources must not exceed the national economy's ability to bear. Local government affairs are progressing with the times, so the need for government expenses, and its revenue, will increase accordingly. The argument for opening up sources of revenue is obvious. However, the national ability to bear is ultimately limited. Once it is exceeded, it is tantamount to destroying the national economy and causing social prosperity to decline. This is what the financial authorities of each province and city should pay close attention to. (Proposed by the National Government Accounting Office)

(Topic) Provinces may not re-levy taxes on goods that have already been subject to the central consolidated tax. (Methods) It was found that in the past, when provincial governments or military agencies re-levied taxes on goods subject to consolidated tax, the Ministry would issue orders or instructions to stop them, but there were no strict measures to crack down on them. It is now proposed that, in addition to requesting the National Government to issue a general order to the provincial governments and military commanders to investigate and determine the re-levy situation under their jurisdiction and prohibit it within a time limit, the National Government should also clearly stipulate punitive measures for re-levying consolidated tax and promulgate them for implementation. If county and city governments or local organizations re-levy taxes, the provincial finance department should be responsible for refunding the amount in full and deducting the county and city governments' administrative expenses to compensate in order to maintain the tax system and provide a warning. (Topic) Abolish local surcharges under tobacco and alcohol categories. (Methods) All tobacco and alcohol surcharges in various provinces are close to being arbitrary taxes and levies and are listed for abolition in the previous National Finance Conference resolution. It is not appropriate to delay it for a long time, which would hinder tax administration. As the fiscal year begins, provinces should quickly find other ways to compensate within the scope of local taxes so that provincial bureaus can be ordered to immediately stop collecting the aforementioned tobacco and alcohol surcharges. Areas that have not implemented surcharges should not take the opportunity to do so to alleviate merchants' difficulties and comply with the original plan. (The above proposals are from Wu Qiding, Director of the Tax Administration).

Results of U.S. Recovery Investigation, Advocate Industrial Socialism, Current Recovery Regulations Favor Large Industrialists, But Disadvantage Small Businesses and Consumers 20

(Washington) The report of Mr. Tai Luo, Chairman of the U.S. Recovery Investigation Department, was submitted to President Roosevelt today. The report suggests that the socialization of industry is the only way to save the economic panic. The report is more than 80,000 words long and is based on a detailed investigation of the regulations of the National Recovery Administration. Mr. Tai Luo's main criticisms of the recovery regulations are as follows: (1) The Recovery Administration encourages monopolies and oppresses small businesses; (2) Some industry regulations are poorly implemented; (3) The recovery regulations are detrimental to consumers. The report puts forward several suggestions, advocating that the United States should adopt socialism, implement industrial control policies, and then adopt a planned economy to develop the resources of the United States. It also advocates that the implementation of industry regulations should be transferred from the Recovery Administration to the Federal Trade Commission, and that the anti-trust law should be restored, which is considered a matter of urgency. It also said that the formation of a monopoly in the American steel industry is extremely dangerous for ordinary consumers. The recovery regulations are a illusory experiment and are unable to stop rampant competition, which is harmful to some industries. Mr. Johnson, Director of the Recovery Administration, and Mr. Lei Bai, who is in charge, wrote to President Roosevelt, regarding Mr. Tai Luo's report as absurd and impractical, and advocating the abolition of the Recovery Investigation Department. (20th, National Dispatch)

(Washington) The National Recovery Investigation Committee released a report today, totaling 80,000 words, with some criticisms of the National Recovery Administration. This committee was established by President Luo to investigate whether industry regulations promote patents, or eliminate or oppress small-scale operators. The leader of this committee is the famous lawyer Mr. Da Luo. After its establishment, it received 113 petitions against 18 types of industry regulations and conducted investigations. The report has now been released, stating that the so-called fair competition is only an illusion. What strong producers call fair is exactly what weak competitors denounce as extremely unfair. There is no way to reconcile the views of the two sides. All competition is barbaric and cruel, and there is no such thing as fairness. The report advocates restoring the anti-trust law in order to restore competition, which is considered one of the urgent needs of the times. The report said that setting prices for industries and regulating prices by the government have the same difficulties. Managing industries to prevent price competition is a tool that the American public has long relied on to avoid the malpractices of patents, the inefficiency of businesses, and the increase in prices. However, this problem cannot be overcome in the end. The report then described various industries, saying that measures to monopolize film and television films are unscrupulous, and small-scale businesses are being oppressed. The state of steel industry patents has existed for a long time. The reason is the absolute dominance of large-scale companies. Although the American Iron and Steel Association represents large and small steel industries, in practice, its voting system allows small-scale steel industries to rely on the whims of large-scale ones and listen to their dominance. Therefore, the dominance of large companies is increasingly consolidated due to the Iron and Steel Association. The above conclusions are the opinions of the majority of the committee members. However, Mr. Xing Kelai, a writer on economics and finance, does not think so and has prepared a separate report. Mr. Da Luo and Mr. Tang Musen have additional reports, saying that forcing restrictions on production in order to maintain high prices, this kind of approach has absolutely no hope of the revival or complete recovery of small industrialists. What the American people, including small industrialists, hope for is to make good use of American resources based on socialization. If the government allows large-scale ones to maintain their interests, then this is not a planned economy, but an organization aimed at exploiting and benefiting itself. If the power of the National Recovery Administration is handed over to the Federal Trade Commission, then the public can be slightly informed of the difficulties faced by small industries in the current stage of industrial development and in the capital structure of the United States. After Mr. Da Luo's report was released, General Johnson, Director of the Recovery Administration, immediately sent a letter to President Luo to refute it, pointing out that this report was a superficial, willful and incorrect document, and advocated immediately abolishing this investigation committee because it was of no benefit to anyone, but was an organ of political law. It also said that the investigation committee was based on biased petitions and hastily judged industry regulations that had been studied and investigated by the Recovery Administration for several weeks in just a few hours. If such an organ is allowed to continue to exist, it will promote private actions and hinder the public. It is already clear that this investigation has not been able to perform its duties. (20th, Reuters Dispatch)

(New York) After the National Recovery Investigation Committee released its report, most newspapers criticized it. The New York Times said that the original plan of the National Recovery Administration was to formulate industry regulations for a small number of major industries, but now it has spread to all industries, which is inevitably cumbersome. This is beyond the capabilities of any bureaucratic agency. It is hoped that the industry regulations that can and cannot be implemented will be greatly eliminated in the future. The Commercial Daily said that the report of the National Recovery Investigation Committee has shown that the commentators have a left-leaning tendency. They openly advocate turning industry into a shared system. People like Mr. Da Luo, Chairman of the Investigation Committee, are almost candidates for the seat of Lenin in the United States. According to Reuters Washington, Mr. Da Luo's friends claimed today that Mr. Da Luo was not asked to defend the Yin Suer case. Mr. Da Luo did not want to be involved in legal cases again, but hoped that the National Recovery Investigation Report would be his last great work. (21st, Reuters Dispatch)

Soviet Union's Far East Economy, Five-Year Plan Develops Rapidly 26

(TASS News Agency, Khabarovsk, April 22) During the first five-year plan, the Soviet Far East invested 900 million rubles in new construction. This year, socialist construction in various departments will have a broader development. The total investment this year is 1.8 billion rubles, including 474 million for industry, more than 54 million for agriculture, and 695 million for transportation and telecommunications. Geological surveys in recent years have proven that the coal reserves in the Tie'ermobulieyingse district exceed 100 million tons and are now being prepared for mining. Large iron ore deposits (approximately 500 million tons) have been discovered in the Lesser Khingan Mountains near the Bulieyingse coal area. This ore can be the foundation for the construction of a metallurgical plant at the end of the 11th five-year plan. Large non-ferrous metal and rare metal deposits have also been discovered in the Far East. The industrial development of the region is very rapid. Huge factories such as the Sibasike Cement Plant, the Sukhanovsky Shipyard, and the Khabarovsk Oil Refinery are all under construction. At the same time, electrical plants in Aoke, Heilongjiang, Khabarovsk, Nikolsk Ussuriysk and elsewhere are also under construction. A shipyard is being built on the Heilongjiang River. The multi-metal plant in Tuideke, one of the largest multi-metal plants in the Soviet Union, has started manufacturing non-ferrous metals. The progress in agriculture is also very considerable. Wheat, rice, and soybeans have been cultivated in the grasslands of the Ussuri River and the Heilongjiang River. The mechanization of agricultural labor is progressing very rapidly. The number of tillage machines used this year exceeds 19 times that of 1927. Fifty-one state-run farms for planting soybeans have been established. The Soviet coastal areas such as Sakhalin, Okhotsk, and Kamchatka are changing rapidly. Coastal areas have become fishing centers, and fishing results have exceeded seven times those of 1913. Many canned fish factories have been established. There are now quite a few state-run livestock farms. The number of deer herds has tripled in the past three years. Six scientific livestock stations have been established in the area, each covering one million hectares. The Far East timber accounts for 5% of the world's reserves. For development purposes, dozens of state-run enterprises were established during the first five-year plan. The timber harvested in 1929 was 2 million cubic meters, and in 1933 it was more than 3 million cubic meters. The development of transportation in the area is also receiving great attention. There is a regular flight between Khabarovsk, the capital of the area, and Sakhalin. The final construction of the Moscow-Khabarovsk airline will begin this year. An airline will also be opened from Vladivostok to Petropavlovsk Kamchatsky, a distance of 4,000 kilometers. The urban population of the region has doubled since the revolution. More than 500,000 workers and employees are involved in the industry of the region.

Telegram from Kashgar Refugees: Situation of Turmoil in Southern Xinjiang, Marshal Ma Shaowu's Forces Defeat the Khotan Rebels 35

(Nanjing) The representatives of Kashgar refugees telegraphed the central government, stating that the turmoil in southern Xinjiang has lasted for a year. At first, the rebels of Bogu took political reform as their goal. Although they committed many atrocities against the Han and Hui people within the customs, they still had some scruples. Later, it developed into a racial war, in which all Han and Hui people were targeted for slaughter. The surviving Han and Hui people concentrated in Akland, Shufu, Shule, Shache, and He'a counties to resist the rebels. Deaths piled up day after day, gradually decreasing the population. Only Shule City, under the command of Kashgar District Administrative Chief Ma Shaowu, led the military and civilians to fight bloody battles with the rebels, struggling to hold on until now. Shufu is connected to Shule. During the summer and autumn of last year, our army advanced several times to provide assistance, but due to the weakness of our forces, we gained and lost the territory repeatedly. At the beginning of January this year, Khotan rebel leader Hoja Niyaz, who initiated the rebellion in Kucha, indeed arrived in Shule and established a stronghold, employing Turkish adventurers to plan for him. He then established the fake state of "East Turkestan," organized a government, and issued propaganda in the hopes of breaking away from the Republic of China. He also purchased several thousand Austrian-made Water-Lian Zhu rifles and many machine guns with over 70,000 head of cattle and sheep to besiege Shule, which was extremely fierce. Fortunately, Administrative Chief Ma's command was appropriate, and after years of hard fighting, he was not able to succeed. On February 6th, he summoned Ma Zhongying's subordinates Ma Bu-yuan and others to lead their troops to Kashgar, and launched an internal and external attack, which finally defeated the Khotan rebels. Shule was relieved from the siege, and Shufu was also recovered immediately. This remaining isolated city, which is the only fruit of our struggle, has been able to maintain a few survivors. It is truly fortunate that the remaining Han and Hui people in the entire county have been able to coexist temporarily. However, the rebel forces are strong and powerful, and we are unable to completely eliminate them. We are isolated internally and externally, with no way to call for assistance. If we delay any longer, we will inevitably be annihilated by the rebels. The lives of these thousands of people are not worth regretting, but the territory of hundreds of miles may become a continuation of the four northeastern provinces. How can we not be in pain? We humbly request the government to consider the importance of border defense, to telegraph Ambassador Yan to find ways to stop the supply of weapons to the rebels and to quickly send reinforcements in the hope of completely eliminating the rebels to save us from danger and death. We are extremely grateful. Representatives of Kashgar Refugees: Zhang Xianyao, Yang Qingming, Lu Shaozhou, Tao Mingrong, Li Qikang, Cai Zhongdao, Zhang Shusong, Yu Luqing, Xie Menglin, Wang Jiantang, Dong Guangzi, Mei Bing [Special Dispatch, 21st]

The Judicial Yuan Issues a Circular to the Courts, Explaining the Conditions for Provisional Attachment 63

(Nanjing) The Judicial Yuan issued a circular to the courts, stating that provisional attachment should not be made unless there is a risk of compulsory execution in the future, etc. If only someone denies an already registered mortgage right, it is not a reason for difficulty in execution, because after the mortgage right is registered, it has the effect of countering third parties. If there is indeed a mortgage right and there are no other reasons for difficulty in execution, there is still no need for provisional attachment. [Special Dispatch, 21st]

International Commercial Telegram 93

Reuters special commercial dispatch, May 21

Silver Prices 94

New York: The silver market opened stable and quiet today (21st) due to the closure of many overseas markets. Sentiment remains positive, but expectations for President Roosevelt's message on silver led to a slight loosening of the market. However, the profit-taking by a small number of speculators was absorbed.

Bombay: The Bombay silver price closed stable today (21st), with spot prices at 53 rupees 13 annas, the same as the previous closing price. Futures prices also remained unchanged.

Exchange Rates 95

US-UK: The New York exchange rate for British pounds today (21st) was $5.10075, the same as the 23rd. The 45th was $5.1005.

US-France: The New York exchange rate for French francs today (21st) was 6.6100.

Cotton Market 96

US Cotton: The cotton market opened with no excitement today (21st). Merchants are awaiting President Roosevelt's message to Congress on silver. Retail brokers were selling in the South, while industry insiders and the Far East were buying. Later, due to the lack of new developments and profit-taking by bulls, and because of favorable weather, prices fell slightly.

Indian Cotton: In the Bombay cotton market today (21st), Continental European exporters and speculators were buying, while futures traders were selling. At 5:30 PM, the price for the July-August contract for Galot cotton was 196 rupees, one rupee lower than Friday's closing price.
