Kashgar Bandits in Xinjiang Flee into Great Snow Mountain 丨Our Army Halts Pursuit Due to Proximity to Russian Border丨 108

Special Dispatch from Kashgar: Following the rebellion in Hami, Xinjiang, the bandit leader Hoja Niyaz, after being defeated by provincial troops in the Zhenxi area of Hami last year, led the remnants to harass Shanshan and Turpan in the Southern Route. They fought fiercely with the provincial troops on several occasions and suffered heavy losses. Subsequently, it was reported that they had surrendered to the provincial troops. After a period of reorganization, they rebelled again, harassing Yanqi, Kucha, Aksu, and other places. They purchased a large quantity of guns and ammunition from a certain country in exchange for cattle and sheep, transported from Hara Lake to Ush-Bel to receive them. The bandits' ambitions revived, and they established a false state and organized a false government in Shufu. They sent dozens of representatives to a certain country to continue purchasing guns, ammunition, and aircraft, intending to secede from the Republic of China. In early February of this year, after being severely suppressed by Kashgar Administrative Director Ma Shaowu, the bandits scattered. Recently, they have been gathering remnants in Artush and attempting a comeback. Director Ma designed an encirclement, killing many. The latest details are revealed below:

After the bandit lair in Shufu was broken, the remnants retreated toward Yingjisha and Shache. On March 9, they fled to the Artush area, about 70 li from Shufu. Director Ma sent commanders Ma Fuyuan and Ma Wenli to lead troops to suppress them. After a fierce battle of about five hours, the bandit forces gradually weakened.

After being defeated, the Hoja bandit fled into the Hetush West Valley and was surrounded by our army. By 2 PM on the 10th, about 2,500 were killed, over 600 guns were seized, and a large amount of other military supplies was captured.

Due to heavy casualties, the bandit leader fled toward the border with only a few dozen followers via a small mountain path. Our army pursued and attacked, and by the evening of the 11th, the bandits entered the Great Snow Mountain. Because of the proximity to the Soviet border post, they did not dare to pursue further. (Dispatch from Shufu, 23.3.15)

National Finance Conference: Gao Bingfang of the Secretariat Greets Journalists and Reports on Key Conference Points 109

The Secretariat of the National Finance Conference greeted the press at 3 PM on the 19th. Gao Bingfang reported: (1) The Secretariat has received a total of 75 proposals so far. The content can be summarized as "practical and detailed." In particular, the accompanying investigation forms and registers are treasures that various parties have been unable to obtain in the past. Although we cannot print them all, we will compile a summary into statistical tables and classify and display various forms, regulations, etc., in the review room for reference at any time. What is particularly admirable is that none of the experts' proposals are empty theories. They can be said to be "thorough, concise, and practical," truly applying science to the people, and are a dawn of political reform. (2) There are currently 80 registered attendees. All provinces and cities have representatives. All directors and commissioners of finance, except for one or two who could not attend due to unavoidable circumstances, have rushed to attend. The financial commissioners of border provinces such as Gansu and Ningxia have already traveled thousands of miles. The enthusiastic attendance of members also proves the importance of this conference. (3) The conference schedule has been seen in various newspapers. The intention is to focus on detailed discussions in the review committee because local finance is different from central finance, and the situation in each province is different. It cannot be "forcing conformity by mutilating" [Procrustean]. To ensure that it can be implemented, it is necessary to discuss it at length. Even the cases submitted by the Ministry only state the outline and do not harbor prejudices. We hope that all members will contribute their opinions as much as possible, and any workable method is a good method. Various proposals will be published successively, so there is no need to "jump the gun." (4) But there is one point that you often ask about and must be answered briefly. This conference focuses on reducing land tax surcharges and abolishing exorbitant taxes and levies. The provinces will certainly demand compensation. How to deal with this difficult problem? In fact, not many provinces have this request, and even if they do, it is not for this reason. Why? Because (A) the evils of exorbitant taxes are due to the poor tax laws, and the burden on the people is not equal. As long as there is a good way to reorganize, the evils will be eliminated and the tax revenue will not decrease, or may even increase the land tax. (B) The evils of exorbitant taxes lie in disturbing the people and mostly arise from poor collection methods. If the collection methods can be improved, the evils of disturbing the people will be eliminated, and the tax revenue will not be affected. For example, the various taxes collected by contractors are obvious examples. (C) Not only is extravagance in expenditure inappropriate, but also unrestricted expenditure is useless even if there is compensation. Therefore, limiting expenditure means saving money. (D) The public revenue from truly exorbitant taxes is actually not much. There is no need to worry about not being able to compensate. Cutting a large pile only reduces a small amount of money. Therefore, by reorganizing good taxes, evenly distributing the burden, eliminating corruption, and adjusting expenditure, exorbitant taxes will be abolished without being abolished. The talk of compensation is actually an excessive worry due to a lack of understanding of the situation. (5) Therefore, the goal of this conference is to focus on the active words "reorganization" and not on the passive words "abolition." This is the answer to your daily questions. (6) As for the supply of news materials for this conference, we intend to make it as convenient and quick as possible so that you will not suffer the pain of chasing. The main methods are as follows: 1. Prepare more printed materials for distribution. 2. Designate certain personnel, certain places, and certain times. 3. Whether it is a general meeting or a review meeting, anything that can be announced will be written in advance and distributed to the newspapers, which is doubly more convenient than reporters inquiring on their own. This method is both our wish and also because the meeting place is too small, so we ask you to forgive us and rest assured. The detailed methods will be discussed in detail with you by the two sections of agenda and communication.

Explosion at Hong Kong Gas Company 110

Over a Hundred People Killed and Injured

Losses Under Investigation

Hong Kong Communication: The No. 1 gas holder of the Hong Kong Gas Company in Sai Wan exploded suddenly on the 15th, affecting the houses in Carron Terrace, Chentin Street, and Yu On Terrace, which were all burned down, totaling more than thirty buildings.

The Hong Kong Gas Company Explosion

The number of people killed and injured is about one hundred, and many are missing. It is truly a great disaster. The disaster area was rescued by firefighters at the time, and post-disaster work began on the 16th. Firefighters, the Cleansing Bureau, and coolies cooperated to excavate, remove the bodies of those crushed, and erect scaffolding to support the collapsed houses. Work continued for several days. A total of eighty-eight injured people were admitted to the hospital for treatment and died in the hospital. Twenty-one people died in the hospital, and sixty-seven people were injured. Thirty-five people have been discharged from the hospital after recovering, and thirty-two are still in the hospital. Currently, the Hong Kong government and various charitable organizations are actively providing relief to the victims and investigating the losses in the disaster area. However, in order to prevent danger in the future, the issue of relocating the coal mine is also being discussed. It is reported that the gas holder will be moved to Sham Shui Po across the sea. The gas company has already purchased a large piece of open space in Sham Shui Po. If the relocation is realized in the future, a large gas pipe will be built at sea, roughly placed around the seawater pipe, to transport gas to Hong Kong for civilian use. The Sai Wan gas company will be used for coal storage and a small gas holder will be retained to supply gas. However, this matter cannot be realized without three years. (18th)

Budget Proposal of Fujian Province 111

Annual Deficit of Over Five Million

Party Fees Reduced to 240,000

Fuzhou Communication: The local revenue and expenditure budget proposal for the 23rd year of the Republic of Fujian Province has been approved by the Provincial Government Committee. The annual revenue and expenditure difference is more than five million yuan. Although the Ministry of Finance has agreed to subsidize 3.6 million yuan annually, there is still a shortage of about 1.8 million yuan. Recently, the Minhou Tax Bureau has been trying to expand tax sources, even taxing milking cows, selling fresh flowers, selling cigarettes, and weaving towels, causing poor farmers and small merchants to oppose it. The income is still very small. The provincial government has to vigorously implement streamlining of administration. The expenses of various institutions can only be paid at most at 70%. All construction, education, and new policies are temporarily shelved. The most significant reduction is in party affairs expenses, which have been reduced from 400,000 yuan to 240,000 yuan annually, which has been reported to the Nanchang Headquarters for approval. Chen Zhaoying, special commissioner for party affairs in the province, stated that when Yang Shuzhuang was the chairman of Fujian Province, the annual party fees were set at 600,000 yuan. When Fang Shengtao was the acting chairman, they were reduced to 480,000 yuan. When Chiang Kwang-nai was the chairman, they were reduced to 360,000 yuan. Now they have been reduced to 240,000 yuan. The expenses of the provincial party headquarters alone require 12,000 yuan per month, leaving only 8,000 yuan. Distributing this to the counties is not enough, so the party affairs guidance commissioners in various districts, even though they have taken office, cannot go to work. The party affairs cadres in various counties, even though they have completed their training, cannot be assigned. The party affairs in the entire province have fallen into a state of stagnation. However, since this case was decided by the Nanchang Headquarters, the provincial government cannot change it. Chen Zhaoying decided to go to Nanjing and Nanchang within a few days to report on the situation of party affairs in Fujian Province to the central government and the headquarters, requesting that the original budget be restored, otherwise he will resign and no longer come to Fujian. The reason why the budget difference in Fujian Province this year is so large is because the newly compiled 15 regiments of the Security Corps by the Security Department require a monthly expenditure of 300,000 yuan for military pay, plus various bandit suppression fees and temporary fees, which also require 100,000 yuan per month, which was not the case in previous years. Xu Fu, the current director of finance, has decided to take the Wanhsiang steamer to Shanghai and then to Nanjing today (15th) to participate in the National Finance Conference and request relief measures from the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance. (May 15th)

A request has been submitted to the provincial government to order the Huangshan Construction Committee to designate a small school site in each area, requiring 40 to 60 mu of land, and to reserve an open space of 100 to 120 mu in a suitable location for large-scale summer lectures, public sports grounds, or military training and public gatherings in the future. Songjiang: Shen Diaoyang and Others Request the Dispatch of Personnel to Inspect River Works (Telegram) 114

To Chen Min, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and Yu Jun, Commissioner of Civil Affairs: The committee meeting for this dredging project has only been held twice, and the budget contract has not yet been submitted for discussion. Construction started on March 7 of the lunar calendar and has been underway for a month. The county magistrate and district chiefs remain aloof and have not set foot on the riverbank. The water in the first section of the project is three feet deep and has never been drained. The earthwork is not being taken from the bottom of the river but is only being excavated from the slopes half a wen away from the middle waterline, causing the banks to collapse everywhere and the river channel to narrow, unable to accommodate two boats. Small dams are erected every ten zhang or so, only removing the topsoil from the water surface, leaving the water full of earthen ridges. The river workers arbitrarily pile up mud, trampling on gardens and blocking houses. The foreman does not know the names of the workers and cannot stop them. Now, most of the river workers have been dismissed, and the work is not even half done, but it has already stopped. Water is needed for farming, and delays cannot be tolerated. Local representatives have repeatedly requested the county magistrate to inspect and supervise, but he does not respond to telegrams and cannot be seen when visited. River works are fundamental to the livelihood of a place. The provincial government has actively built it and allocated a large amount of money, originally with the intention of caring for the people, but who knew that it would only become a stage for a few corrupt officials to live in luxury and divide the profits. If this is not punished, what use is the national law? In desperation, we telegraphed Your Excellency, hoping that you would be furious, quickly remove and punish them, and appoint capable personnel to inspect and supervise, ordering the completion of the work within a limited time. The local people will be fortunate. Citizens of the first section of the Songjiang River Works: Shen Diaoyang, Sun Yangxing, Zhu Boke, Wang Guchang, Gu Wenyao, Gu Yangchu, respectfully,

Frequent Robberies in Various Townships 115

Recently, bandits have sprung up in various townships, and robbery cases have occurred frequently. Almost every day there is news of them. In Zhoujiacao, seven or eight li from the city, more than a dozen bandits suddenly came to the homes of Lu Baoquan and others at about 11 PM last night (20th). They were wearing tattered military uniforms and carrying handguns. They searched each household, threatening the victims, who dared not speak up and allowed them to plunder and leave. They then went to the homes of Shen Xiuhong, Shen Longgen, Mugen, and Guan Chang in the neighboring village of Shenxiuhong, wantonly robbing them and escaping with the stolen goods. Six houses were robbed on the same night, with losses of over a thousand yuan. The victims provided a list of losses and reported it to the Songjiang aquatic police today, requesting them to pursue the bandits and sending personnel to investigate. Also, in the Liuhe Temple area near Xinqiao, more than a dozen bandits came at about 12 PM the night before last. They spoke with a Hakka accent. They first robbed the Shen Hongsheng family, then the Cai Zhengrong, Wang Caigen, Xia Sanhe, and Wang Jusheng families, robbing for about two hours. They plundered stolen goods and, before leaving, stole a farmer's boat, loaded it, and escaped, firing several shots as a warning.

Public Security Bureau Investigates Opium Addicts 116

The Regulations for the Organization of the Provincial Anti-Smoking Committee have been promulgated, ordering each county to begin establishing the committee starting in June, with the county magistrate and the director of the Public Security Bureau as ex officio members, and joining three local people to form a committee to handle anti-smoking matters in name, but actually implement the public sale of opium. The county government has received a provincial order to prepare immediately and ordered the Public Security Bureau today to investigate addicts and report the register before the 25th. The Public Security Bureau has already gone to the township offices to borrow household registers and has begun investigating each household.

Suzhou: Peng Guoyan Escorted to Suzhou 117

Peng Guoyan, who ranked first in the first county magistrate examination in Jiangsu Province, first governed Wuxian County and achieved remarkable results. He was impeached due to his direct opposition to the former Commissioner of Civil Affairs, Miao Bin, and was arrested by the provincial government. When Miao left office, Peng served as the county magistrate of Jiangyin and Pixian. Later, while serving in Peixian, he was again detained by the former Commissioner of Civil Affairs, Zhao Qi, and imprisoned in the provincial government for two years. He was only sent to the Zhenjiang District Court for trial until the reorganization of the provincial government. Peng did not accept the conviction and sentence of the Zhenjiang District Court and appealed to the Suzhou High Court. He was escorted to Suzhou by bailiff Zhang Buyun from the Zhenjiang District Court last night (21st) to await trial by the Suzhou High Court. It is heard that the Suzhou High Court is now scheduled to open the trial on June 2nd.

Mishap Caused by Water Police Extorting Illegal Fees 118

It is said that on the 20th, villagers in Chehe Bridge, Wuli, Chefang, held a ceremony to thank the gods and performed a play. The Fifth Squad of the Water Police stationed in Xietang dispatched 14 police officers to suppress it. It happened that the villagers there were gambling together. Because the extortion of illegal fees was not successful, they implemented a ban, resulting in a conflict. The villagers gathered and surrounded the water police. The water police fired warning shots into the air, and the villagers dispersed in panic. Unexpectedly, the Second Squad of the Second Company of the County Police and the Third Squad of the County Water Patrol, which were stationed there, rushed to investigate after hearing the gunshots. The villagers regained their courage and used huge stones to throw at the water police patrol boat. The water police fired again, injuring a carpenter named A Wu. He was taken to see a doctor yesterday (21st). Currently, this case, caused by the water police arresting gamblers outside their jurisdiction, is still under negotiation and has not been resolved.

Director Shen Jian Inspects the Su-Chang Road 119

Shen Baixian, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction, taking into account the imminent opening of the Seven-Province Transportation Exhibition, took a car the day before yesterday to inspect the Ju-Piao, Xi-Yi, and Xi-Cheng roads along the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway. The day before yesterday, he came to Suzhou from Wuxi. Yesterday (21st) at 8:00 am, he set off by steamboat with Director Zhou of the Construction Bureau to inspect the Pingqi section of the Ring Road and the Su-Chang Road, which are under construction. He returned to the city at 4:00 pm. The roadbed of the road has been 50% completed, and 24 bridges are under construction simultaneously, roughly taking shape. It is estimated that all of them can be completed in about ten days. Shen plans to return to Zhenjiang after inspecting the Su-Jia Road.

Wuxi: Ma Shuxiang Continuously Robs and Injures People 120

Lu Xingbao, a resident of Ma Shuxiang near Yanjiaqiao in the Eighth District (Huai Xia City) of the county, works as a farmer and is diligent and frugal. He has some savings, which are coveted by bandits. At about 12:00 pm the night before last (20th), four bandits suddenly came to Lu's house, speaking with a northern accent, each holding a pistol, wearing blue cloth short shirts and pants, looking like workers. They broke into the house, dragged Xingbao from the bed, forced him to drink liquor, and forced him to tell where the silver was hidden. Then they rummaged through boxes and cabinets, arbitrarily robbing them. The bandits were not satisfied, and went to Wang Quansheng's house in the neighboring house to rob, and burned Quansheng's face and other places with fire. After about an hour, they left with the loot, shouting and escaping. Afterwards, the Wang and Lu families checked the losses, totaling five to six hundred yuan.

Child Bride Runs Away and is Raped 121

Meiyun (nickname Dejin), the second daughter of Cheng Ziyou, a villager in Huashu Town, Jiangyin County, is currently fifteen years old. Since childhood, she was betrothed to the son of Zhao Baochu (Laqi) in the same village by her parents. She was brought into the family as a child bride. Because she could not bear the hardships of life in her husband's family, she ran away to Wuxi and lived in the home of her paternal uncle Cheng Dan'an on Wantou, outside the South Gate. Later, her father Cheng Ziyou found out and planned to take Meiyun back. Meiyun was unwilling, so she took the opportunity to jump into the courtyard of the neighboring Fang Hexing Copper and Iron Workshop, and then escaped again. When she walked near the Nanshuixian Temple, she met a woman named Zhang from the same village, who took Meiyun into her home. Zhang lived in a thatched shed behind the Nanshuixian Temple and had a lover named Zhang Dekui, who was a peddler. Unexpectedly, Dekui saw that Meiyun was beautiful, and had an improper thought. On the night of the 16th of this month, he forcibly raped Meiyun. Meiyun, feeling that she was in a difficult situation and could not live there, ran away again and stayed overnight in the Shuixian Temple. Yesterday, Zhang Dekui found out and planned to take her back again. Meiyun refused, causing a dispute. It happened that Police Chief Liu Desheng of the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau saw it and took the two to the bureau, and ordered Zhang to come to the bureau. Investigator Sun held a preliminary hearing. Meiyun confessed the experience of being raped. Dekui and Zhang denied it. Investigator Sun, seeing that the two sides had different versions of the story, ordered them to be temporarily detained together and wait for Meiyun's family to come to the case for questioning before further investigation.

Jiading: Japanese Navy Lieutenant Comes to Jiading 122

More than 70 members of the Japanese Shanghai Special Naval Landing Force came to Jiading some time ago. As of the 25th of this month, on the 20th, Lieutenant Lin Kazuo of the Japanese Navy, along with a dozen officers, took three cars from Shanghai to Jiading. Lin and four officers took one car and arrived at the station at 10 am. The station police reported it, and the County Public Security Bureau dispatched inspectors You Zhiliang and Jiang Jiwu to inquire. They claimed to be here for sightseeing and there were no incidents. When asked for their passports, they could not provide them, so You and others followed and monitored them into the city. Later, the remaining officers arrived in two cars and left after a short stay. Lin and others entered the city from Dongda Street to Zhou Bridge and returned. They went to the City God Temple and visited inside for about an hour, then returned to Shanghai in the original car.

A floating corpse suddenly appeared in Yujiaogang, One District, last month. It was seen by villagers Wang Ruohua and Zhu Xianglang. A Joke Turns into a Murder Case 128

Wang Nengjin, the son of Wang Deyu, a farmer in Dahong Town, Three District, is seventeen years old. The day before yesterday (17th), he was weeding in the field with Jiang Tingxuan's son Zhixian. Because they were joking with each other, Zhixian accidentally stabbed Nengjin in the abdomen with a knife, about an inch deep. Blood flowed like a fountain, and he fell to the ground in extreme pain. Zhixian, seeing that he had caused a disaster, fled without regard for anything. Later, his family found out, carried him to Haimen Hospital for treatment, but the injury was too severe and the medicine was ineffective. He died yesterday. His family should report to the county government for an autopsy. Today (19th) at 10:00 am, the body was carried to the Doutian Temple in the county city, where Deng Cheng, the coroner, went to perform the autopsy. He confirmed that he had died from being stabbed. He ordered the family to bury the body and arrest the murderer for investigation.

Huzhou: Police Officers Bleed While Cracking Down on Vendors 130

Recently, the Wuxing County Public Security Bureau, due to the proliferation of vendors on the streets, which hindered traffic, specially dispatched Traffic Police Patrol Chief Liu Shaochun and four police officers, including Xu Bin, to drive away vendors in various places. At about 3:00 pm, they checked the entrance of the Yongxing Rattan Shop in Zhicheng Road and saw rattan chairs and other appliances placed in front of the door. The police officers ordered them to be moved inside. Unexpectedly, the number of spectators gradually increased at this time, and a quarrel arose due to a misunderstanding amidst the noisy voices. Then they started fighting. Police Officer Xu Bin was injured in the head, and blood flowed straight down. Another police officer dragged Xu out of the siege and helped him to the bureau. At this time, the guard police at the site saw this and immediately called the county bureau to request that police be sent to maintain order. After receiving the call, the bureau sent Patrol Officer Wang and three squads of armed student police. The spectators had already scattered. The shop assistant of Yongxing Rattan Shop, Lu Zhaosheng, was arrested and taken to the bureau. However, the shops there saw that the police officers were arresting people and felt injustice. All the shops from Zhicheng Road to Xuanhuafang, Yishang Street, and the entrance of Guanyixiang, and from Caifengfang to Yangxiangkou, closed one after another, and reported to the County Chamber of Commerce to preside over the matter. After receiving the report, the chamber of commerce issued a notice to persuade the shops to open in order to avoid losses. The injured police officer Xu Bin has been sent to Huzhou Hospital for treatment by the county bureau. It is said that the police officer lost too much blood from his head and the injury was quite serious.

The collapsed cart moved forward to the left, and there was no time to avoid it. He was knocked down and both legs were broken, and blood flowed like a fountain. Only the two stevedores were detained in the police station, and the injured person was sent to the hospital for treatment. Because the injury was too serious, he died on the way. Local News

The United Association of Chinese Cotton Mills Issues a Report on the Decline of the Cotton Industry 133

More Than Several Million Spindles Were Shut Down Last Year

The Price of Standard Yarn Fell to More Than One Hundred Yuan

The Inventory of Yarn is Always Over 100,000 Bales

Manufacturers Met Yesterday to Discuss Remedial Measures

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, China's cotton industry has suffered a setback due to the dumping of Japanese yarn and rising flower prices. The National United Association of Chinese Cotton Mills specially convened a conference yesterday to discuss the situation and report on the past situation of the yarn industry. The Shen Shi News Agency reporter specially explored and recorded the details as follows.

Manufacturer Representatives Meet to Discuss 134

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 pm, the United Association of Chinese Cotton Mills convened representatives from more than 40 Chinese cotton mills in this city at its clubhouse on Avenue Edward VII to hold a conference. Nie Lusheng, Xue Runsheng, Xue Chunsheng, Huang Shoumin, Guo Shun, Chen Zixin, Xu Zongtang, Chen Gengxin, and dozens of others attended. Nie Lusheng was elected chairman to discuss issues related to the improvement of the cotton mills themselves, and to make concrete remedial measures based on the current production situation. The discussion lasted until 5:00 pm. The various resolutions were not released due to various reasons.

The United Association of Chinese Cotton Mills Issues a Report 135

The United Association of Cotton Mills issued a report on the past situation of the yarn industry at the meeting, stating that the world economic downturn remained the same last year. All sectors of the United Kingdom and the United States cooperated to seek salvation, and there was hope for the recovery of the Soviet Union. However, China was in great difficulty and could be in danger at any time. The economic recovery of Europe and the United States was purely based on monetary policy and trade opportunities. China's monetary and trade status was the opposite. All industries were declining, and the yarn industry was no exception. At this difficult time, it is necessary to unite and strive for survival.

Cotton Mills Across the Country Unanimously Reduce Working Hours 136

Although the number of spindles increased last year, business continued to decline. The government and the cotton industry held repeated meetings to seek remedies. Since April 22, working hours have been unanimously reduced. The purpose was not to raise yarn prices, but because yarn prices were low and sales were sluggish, inventory increased and funds were accumulated, making it impossible to turn around. Therefore, working hours were reduced to reduce production in order to maintain capital. Later, in consideration of the livelihood of workers and local security, work was gradually resumed. During the free shutdown period, a total of 12 factories were completely shut down, with a total of 426,688 spindles. 4 factories were completely shut down at night, with a total of 97,288 spindles. The total reduction rate nationwide was about 23%. Production was still in excess, so there was a move to stop night work again from July 7. In the first half of last year, the number of spindles shut down exceeded half of the total number, and in the second half of the year, more than one million spindles were shut down. The severity of the reduction in working hours can be imagined.

Yarn Prices Decline and Sales Stagnate 137

Since the great flood of 1931, followed by the Liaoning Incident and the Shanghai Incident, banditry has spread and the countryside has collapsed, and sales have decreased dramatically. Cotton goods have fallen even more due to excessive imports, creating the lowest level seen since the founding of the Republic of China. In the autumn and winter of 1919, the high price of 16-count Ren Zhong fine yarn was 230 taels, equivalent to 320 yuan. On April 18 this year, the price of standard cotton yarn fell to 160 yuan and 30 cents, only half of the old price. Its business slump has posed a major threat to textile factories. According to the economic sector's research on the state of domestic industry, the textile industry is the worst, especially cotton spinning. The 1934 edition fell to an index of 35%. Production needs cannot be met. In the past, the inventory of yarn in Shanghai was only 100,000 bales, but last year it was always more than 100,000 bales. Not only were funds stagnant, but it was difficult to even pay interest. Yarn merchants suffered as a result.

Prospects for the Cotton Textile Industry 138

Yarn flowers are falling day by day, yarn inventories are increasing day by day, and international cotton goods are being dumped. Competition between domestic and foreign factories is becoming more and more fierce, and they are under greater threat. China's textile industry is only 20 years old, and internal and external troubles have come together. As for talent cultivation, there is only one Nantong school. As for training laborers, the factory owners have no time to settle the workers. Rationalization and scientification are difficult to achieve. Moreover, the United States is advocating a silver policy, and once it is implemented, it will put China's yarn industry in a desperate situation. Fortunately, the government is concerned and is working hard on reducing working hours, controlling and lending cotton. In the future, if we want to revive the yarn industry, we must cooperate with finance to implement low-interest loans to make up for deficiencies. We also hope that the government will increase tariffs, reduce domestic tax rates, plant cotton to enrich textile raw materials, run textile education to establish technical talents, and crack down on labor unrest to stabilize factories. Only then can it be effective.

Yin Tong, director of the Beining Railway Bureau, went south from Pingnan and arrived at Pu at 10:00 pm on the 21st. At 12:00 pm, he transferred to a train to Shanghai to visit Huang Wei for consultations on the North China issue. He plans to arrive in Washington as soon as possible and will probably make a trip to Europe. Chairman's Address 150

Today, it is a great honor for me to welcome the Qingdao Industrial Delegation to our association for a joyful gathering and conversation. All of you are the backbone of the Qingdao business community. During my previous trip to Qingdao, I may have met some of you, received hospitality, or known you well. Unexpectedly, old friends from afar are reunited here today. As Du Fu said, "What night is tonight? We share this candlelight." Not only am I personally delighted, but I believe all of you share this feeling of joy. However, your visit carries a significant mission and unlimited aspirations. The future development of North China's industry hinges on this trip, making it crucial. Therefore, you certainly cannot linger in Shanghai every day. With brief meetings and frequent departures, I hope you will generously drink a cup of wine to wish you unlimited success in the future. Shanghai is the largest commercial port in central China and a major port in the East. The situation is different from the inland. From an external perspective, the industries of both commerce and manufacturing are undoubtedly better than elsewhere. However, at the same time, the import of foreign goods and the outflow of our country's blood and sweat also make this port a major source of leakage. Moreover, due to the gathering of merchants and goods, the convenience of transportation, the clustering of foreign merchants and industries, and the observation of Chinese and foreign people, this port is implicitly the center representing China. For this reason, since the tenth year of the Republic of China, our association has strived to promote the development of domestic goods, research the improvement of production, connect the domestic goods industry, establish a commodity exhibition hall, and create domestic goods shopping malls in both the north and south, making practical publicity. Fortunately, we have not lagged behind and have received considerable recognition from the national mentality. Furthermore, with the mutual support and cooperation of various domestic goods manufacturers and merchants, we have achieved unexpected results. In recent years, the consumption of domestic goods by our compatriots has increased dramatically. The national dream is gradually awakening. This alone is a glimmer of hope for saving the nation and ensuring its survival. I also heard that since Qingdao's takeover, the sales of domestic goods have risen from zero to one-third of the city's total. After the previous domestic goods exhibition, sales even reached over 400,000 yuan, breaking the record for domestic goods exhibitions. This shows that everything depends on human effort. If we take Qingdao as an example and apply it to other places, the potential is staggering. All of this is the result of the efforts and cooperation of domestic goods manufacturers nationwide, as well as colleagues in the domestic goods store industry. It cannot be concealed. However, this only concerns a small part of domestic goods. As the saying goes, "choosing the tallest among the short" is just to comfort ourselves. If we look at the competition overseas, the amount sold today is just a grain of rice in a granary. We are in a serious international situation, suffering the pain of being cut and carved. We should not boast about our achievements or be content with small gains and willingly fall behind. Therefore, how can all of us in the industrial and commercial world not shoulder our responsibilities, unite, and strive forward? Gentlemen, you must know that compared to the world's trends, our country's industry and commerce today are like a three-year-old child racing against a flying horse. How dangerous! Taking our eastern neighbor as an example, twenty-nine countries are affected by its dumping. Recently, British colonies have even reduced the import of Japanese goods by two-thirds. There are also frequent reports in newspapers about the United States boycotting Japanese goods. With the power of Britain and the United States, their words are sure to be followed. Therefore, there is no doubt that those restricted in the West will be dumped in the East. Moreover, I fear that those who dump goods will unite the whole world to make our country the end of their competition. Sucking our marrow and blood, will our people still have intact skin? Can our country's goods and industry colleagues still steal a day of rest? Therefore, today, besides expressing my sincere welcome and admiration for your enthusiasm, I have several points I hope from you: (1) I heard that in addition to Shanghai, you will visit other ports for inspection. Therefore, wherever you travel, you will arrive in our country's major cities. In the future, I hope to have a comprehensive report on the findings, published nationwide for reference. Furthermore, gentlemen, ask about misfortune, not good fortune. During your inspection, you will inevitably see both strengths and weaknesses. The records in the report should be as accurate as possible. Then the strengths can be encouraged, and the weaknesses can be improved. (2) Our country's commerce and industry are the most underdeveloped in the world. I hope that wherever you travel, you will constantly encourage the people to work hard. It would be even better to make large-scale speeches and concrete regulations. Then, in addition to gaining inspection results for yourselves, you will receive many intangible benefits. (3) I hope to publicize the past history of Qingdao, the situation after the takeover, the current facilities, and future plans on the ground. Because there are many people who care about the Qingdao issue and want to know its current situation. The above three points are what I, in my limited view, offer to you gentlemen. I hope you will adopt and implement them. Finally, you are fulfilling your duties in the industrial and commercial world, traveling tirelessly from afar. Our association's hospitality has been inadequate, and our guidance has been lacking. I deeply regret disappointing your expectations and feel even more apologetic. As for connecting national commercial information with the industrial and commercial world to seek joint research to promote industrial progress, investing in and opening factories to promote Qingdao's prosperity, and planning to exhibit domestic goods or build a domestic goods shopping mall in Qingdao, these major issues, whether urgent or slow, are already in your plans. I will naturally follow you gentlemen. I will not elaborate further. The end.

Zhejiang Construction Department Signs Loan for Highway Construction with Four Banks. First Batch of 400,000 Yuan Remitted from Salt Industry Bank to Zhejiang, Specifically for Completing the Two Major Trunk Roads of Jingmin-Huhang-Guigui. 152

Total Loan Amount 1.2 Million Yuan, Delivered in Three Phases.

Completing the Jingmin-Huhang-Guigui Highways 153

Zhejiang's highways are the best in the country. The roads already built in various counties are as dense as spider webs, and transportation is very convenient. Recently, another telegram was received from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, ordering the accelerated construction of the previously designated Jingmin, Huhang, and Guigui two main lines, to be completed uniformly by the end of June. Currently, the contract has been signed by the representative Salt Industry Bank and the Zhejiang Construction Department. The weekly interest rate is 9%, and it will be remitted in three months. The first batch of 400,000 yuan was transferred by the Mainland, Jincheng, and Zhongnan Banks yesterday, each transferring 100,000 yuan, and handed over to the Salt Industry Bank for remittance to the Zhejiang Construction Department for verification and receipt.

Donggang Heji Company's Celestial Elephant Ship Sinks 157

Hit Nianzi Reef Due to Thunderstorms, Wind, and Fog

Loss of 100,000, Passengers and Crew Unharmed

The Celestial Elephant ship of Donggang Heji Shipping Company, located on the fifth floor of the New Opened River Flour Exchange in the French Concession, encountered a hurricane and thunderstorm at around 4 a.m. the day before yesterday (20th) near the Tongtou Mountain north of the Wenzhou sea area, causing it to hit a reef and sink. Fortunately, the crew and passengers were unharmed. The details of the investigation are recorded below.

(Encountered Thunderstorms and Fog Midway) The Celestial Elephant was originally named Victory, and later belonged to Donggang Company, renamed Donggang. It was unexpected that Donggang Company suffered losses, so the creditor Zhao Yangfu and others reorganized the company, adding the word Heji, and the ship was also renamed Celestial Elephant. The ship had a load of 800 tons and was still young, sailing between Shanghai and Fujian. On the 9th of this month, it loaded passengers and cargo in Shanghai and sailed to Quanzhou and Xiamen. After unloading, it went to Ruian on the 16th to load firewood, charcoal, and groceries to Shanghai. At around 1 a.m. on the 20th, it left Ruian for Shanghai. At around 4 a.m., while passing through the sea area outside Wenzhou near Tongtou Mountain, it suddenly encountered a hurricane, and thunderstorms occurred. There was also heavy fog on the sea, resulting in the loss of driving ability. The whole ship was panicked. In a blink of an eye, the ship hit a reef on Nianzi Reef.

(Arrangements Before the Ship Sank) The shipowner He Shengyang and the first mate Hu Quanxing, seeing that the ship had hit a reef and the bottom of the ship was pierced, seawater was entering, and the whole ship was alarmed. Fortunately, the shipowner comforted them to be calm and not be impatient. When the sky was slightly brighter and the wind and waves were slightly smaller, the sampans prepared on the ship were lowered, first allowing the passengers and crew to leave the ship. The comprador Yang Ziting also went up the mountain with the sampan. At this time, nearby fishing boats also came to help rescue. The shipowner did not leave the ship and go up the mountain until the whole ship sank and he had no choice. The crew and passengers arrived at Ou. The entire crew of the ship was 58 people, and the number of passengers is unknown. They took their own sampans and fishing boats to escape and go up the mountain. The mountain is Tongtou Mountain, about 30 or 40 miles outside Wenzhou, about 80 or 90 miles from Ruian. After going up the mountain, it was already bright, and the stern of the ship was completely sunk to the bottom of the sea. The driving room could still be seen. When the water fell, the bow of the ship rose about three feet. The comprador Yang Ziting hired a fishing boat and first led 23 crew members to Wenzhou. Then the shipowner and passengers also arrived and went to the Siming Guild Hall to rest temporarily. A telegram was sent to Shanghai. Although the ship encountered a dangerous situation, the passengers and crew were unharmed, which can be called a blessing in disguise.

(Insurance and Two Telegrams) The Shanghai Donggang Heji Company received the first telegram from the comprador at 12 o'clock the night before last (20th), and received the second telegram at 1 p.m. yesterday. The ship had previously taken out a peace insurance of 30,000 yuan with the China Ship United Insurance Company at 160 Edouard Road. Therefore, after receiving the accident report, the company immediately copied the original telegram and sent it to the insurance company for formal notification. The insurance company replied by letter that the telegraph code was unclear and would be processed after the captain's report arrived. According to Zhao Yangfu, the manager of Donggang Heji Company, the aftermath of the sinking ship needs to be resolved by the insurance company, and there is no way to deal with it at the moment. The loss this time should be in the range of 100,000 yuan. The two telegrams are recorded below. The first telegram said, "Elephant (i.e., Celestial Elephant) Jia (20th) left Ruian at 1 a.m. At 4 a.m., it hit a reef at Tongtou Mountain in Beitian, and the stern sank. The crew and passengers are unharmed. Twenty-three crew members hired fishing boats to Ou. The rest are on the mountain and the deck, waiting for small boats to find a way. How to deal with this ship, reply quickly. Yang (Ziting) of Wenzhou Siming Guild Hall." The second telegram said, "Xiang Jia, at 4:10 a.m., encountered thunderstorms, wind, and fog on the Ou Mountain Pan, dark tide was rapid, Du Nianzi Reef, tide rose, see driving room, tide fell, see bow of the ship three feet, crew and passengers Ou transferred to Shanghai Yun."

The Handover of the Shanghai-Yantai-Dagu Submarine Cable Line Management Rights by the Ministry Is of Great Significance 158

There are currently two submarine cable lines between Shanghai, Yantai, and Dagu in our country, namely the famous Shanghai-Yantai-Dagu submarine cable line. Both of these submarine cable lines belong to our country. However, the Shanghai-Yantai submarine cable line and the Yantai-Dagu submarine cable line were laid by the foreign-owned Great Northern and Great Eastern Telegraph Companies with advances. Our country's previous telecommunications authorities signed contracts with the two telegraph companies, entrusting them to manage and operate them on our behalf. In order to ensure the integrity of telecommunications sovereignty, the Ministry of Communications decided to take back the above-mentioned submarine cable lines for self-operation on the 20th of this month. It had previously informed the Great Northern and Great Eastern Companies to hand over the submarine cable lines and all machinery, materials, furniture, etc. The Ministry of Communications also ordered the submarine cable line engineers stationed in Shanghai, Yantai, and Tianjin to be responsible for handling the technology and other matters related to the takeover of the submarine cable lines.

History of Operation on Behalf 159

The above-mentioned Shanghai-Yantai-Dagu submarine cable lines operated on behalf of the Great Eastern and Great Northern Companies were originally established by the companies in the Gengzi year of the former Qing Dynasty. They were recovered by our country at a price in the 26th year of Guangxu, but contracts were still signed to entrust the companies to manage and operate them on our behalf. The required expenses were borne by our country. In addition, the companies were allowed to establish telegraph offices in Shanghai, Yantai, and Dagu during the period of operation on behalf, directly receiving and sending public telegrams. In recent years, the Ministry of Communications has long intended to abolish the above-mentioned contracts and take back the submarine cable lines for self-management, but it has not been realized due to various reasons. Until recently, everything was ready, and the technical preparations were also completed. The Ministry of Communications then notified the company that it would take back the management on the 20th of this month.

Significance of the Takeover 160

The abolition of the Shanghai-Yantai-Dagu submarine cable line contract and the recovery of the management rights of the submarine cable line by the Ministry of Communications are of great significance. The Shanghai-Yantai-Dagu submarine cable line is one of the important telegraph lines between northern and southeastern China. It is inappropriate for the right to manage it to fall into the hands of others. Moreover, foreign submarine cable line companies, in our country, currently only the Great Northern and Great Eastern Companies have a telegraph office in Yantai based on the above-mentioned contract, directly receiving and sending telegrams to the public, which is a defect in our country's telecommunications. After the contract is abolished, not only will the submarine cable line be taken back for self-management, but also the telegraph office established by the company in Yantai will be closed at the same time, which is an extremely memorable event in the history of telecommunications.

Self-Managed Telegraph Office 161

After the Shanghai-Yantai-Dagu submarine cable line is taken over, its Shanghai end, which originally connected to the Great Northern and Great Eastern Company on Edouard Road in Shanghai, will be changed to connect to the Shanghai Telegraph Office on Fuzhou Road. In the future, telegrams between Shanghai and various places in the north will be received and processed by the Shanghai Telegraph Office. The Great Northern and Great Eastern submarine cable telegram receiving and sending offices under the jurisdiction of the International Telegraph Bureau of the Ministry of Communications will stop receiving and sending the telegrams from that day. In addition, it is heard that after the Ministry of Communications takes back the above-mentioned submarine cable line, it intends to install a submarine cable booster in the Yantai Bureau so that Shanghai and Tianjin can communicate directly with the submarine cable line, in order to make it particularly fast.

Incomplete Takeover 162

A Dabaisha reporter spoke with a person in charge of the Telegraph Office yesterday, saying that after our side went through the takeover procedures with the Great Northern and Great Eastern Companies, it went quite smoothly, but due to the tight time, in addition to the general negotiation matters being concluded, the takeover of the submarine cable line has not been completely completed, and it is also very troublesome technically. The day before yesterday was Sunday, and yesterday was also Danish Memorial Day, and both the Great Northern and Great Eastern Companies stopped working, so the transfer of the submarine cable line has not been completed. The rumors that there was a refusal to hand over due to certain procedures are all speculation. Currently, our side's sending lines are temporarily transmitted by the Ministry of Communications' original submarine cable lines, but the receiving and sending aspects are slightly crowded. However, it can be completely taken over within the next day or two.

Bean Cakes Shipped to Guangdong Detained, 200,000 to 300,000 Pieces Detained in Shantou, 400,000 to 500,000 Pieces Still in Shanghai 164

Bean cakes produced by various oil pressing factories in this city are mainly sold to South China. Now, because the Guangzhou donation merchant Huifeng Company mistakenly pointed out that they are products of the three northeastern provinces and should be levied an additional fee of 8 cents per 100 catties as imported fertilizer, bean cakes shipped from Shanghai to Shantou have all been detained, totaling 200,000 to 300,000 pieces. As a result, 400,000 to 500,000 pieces of domestically produced bean cakes waiting to be shipped in Shanghai are also stagnant. The various oil pressing factories are greatly affected and are about to be closed. Now, the city Chamber of Commerce has telegraphed the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Guangdong Provincial Government separately to release them. The details are as follows.

Bean Cake Production Volume: According to a survey by Xin Sheng News, there are six factories in Shanghai that produce bean cakes, namely Dayouyu, Changde, Dadexin, Suifeng, Changji, and Lide. There are two factories in Wuxi, Hengde and Runfeng. There is a Xie Feng factory in Changzhou, a Housheng factory in Kunshan, and an oil factory in Hankou. In total, there are 15 factories. The factories are equipped with self-made machines and are sold domestically. Guangzhou and Shantou are the most prosperous. Taking Shanghai as an example, 30,000 pieces of bean cakes can be produced every day, that is, 900,000 pieces can be produced every month.

Raw Materials Required: The raw materials required by each factory, namely soybeans, are all sourced from the five provinces of Shandong, Henan, Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangsu. In recent years, the soybean production in the five provinces has been abundant and surplus everywhere, and the prices are extremely low. Therefore, each factory is completely supplied by them. If northeastern soybean cakes are used, they will be subject to import taxes and more transportation costs, and the cost will be expensive, which will inevitably lead to losses. For example, the soybean materials in the five provinces of Shandong, Henan, etc., the purchase price is 2.7 to 2.9 yuan per 100 catties in the market, and the average price is 2.8 yuan. In addition, the labor cost is 40 cents, and the total value is 3.2 yuan. Nine to ten catties of soybean oil can be extracted in the market, and the average of nine catties is sold at a higher price of 95 cents. Ninety-one catties of bean cake can be produced in the market, and the average of 625 pieces per genuine cake is sold at 1.38 yuan per catty, totaling 2.24 yuan. The total value of oil cake is 3.19 yuan. In this way, the income and expenditure are equal. If soybeans from the eastern province are used, the cost is 3.5 to 3.6 yuan per 100 catties in the market, and the average price is 3.55 yuan. In addition, the labor cost is 40 cents, and the total value is 3.95 yuan. Ten to eleven catties of soybean oil can be extracted in the market, and the average of ten and a half catties is sold at 1.05 yuan, and 51 catties of bean cake can be produced in the market, and the price is also 1.38 yuan, and the total value of oil cake is 3.29 yuan, that is, it will lose 66 cents. Is it reasonable for merchants to use eastern soybeans and voluntarily lose money?

Tax Collection in Guangdong Province: According to the original plan approved by the Southwest Political Affairs Committee, all bean dregs transported from the three northeastern provinces are regarded as imported fertilizer and charged an additional fee of 8 cents per 100 catties. That is, the Guangdong Finance Special Commissioner's Office Announcement No. 6 also stated that it is limited to bean dregs produced in the three northeastern provinces, which is a good policy to protect domestic production. Unexpectedly, the donation merchant Huifeng Company made extra profits beyond the law and forcibly pointed out that domestic products are imported products and must be taxed at 8 cents per 100 catties. The current cost of each bean cake is about 1.2 yuan, and each bean cake is nearly 100 catties. If taxed in this way, the tax will increase by 40 cents per piece, which is nearly 33% of the value. The domestic oil factories will be greatly affected, which will increase the sales of bean cakes in the eastern provinces.

Chamber of Commerce Certificate: The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, after receiving the report from the Miscellaneous Grain and Oil Cake Industry Association and sending the photos of the trademarks of domestic oil cakes to the meeting, immediately sent letters to the Guangdong Provincial Government, the Finance Special Commissioner, and the Youtou City Chamber of Commerce to prove it. The original case roughly stated, "After investigating the factories that manufacture bean cakes, they are all located in Wuxi, Kunshan, and Wujin counties in Jiangsu Province and within the jurisdiction of Shanghai. The soybean materials used are produced in the five provinces of Shandong, Henan, Anhui, Hubei, and Jiangsu, and are taken nearby. There are factories that can be used as evidence, and the facts can be proven. Now, the attached photos and car schedules are sent to you for verification and transferred to the contractor to check one by one. The goods that were mistakenly detained should be returned as soon as possible. If it is considered that there are still matters that must be taken seriously, in the future, bean cakes shipped from Shanghai to Guangdong can be notified by our association to the Miscellaneous Grain Association to issue a certificate to prove the name of the producing factory and the origin of the raw materials. When loading goods to Guangdong each time, they should be carried with them for identification. Please check and implement."

Twenty-Four Tobacco Merchants Request Tax Rate Change (Continued) The Tax Bureau Clarifies Statistical Errors by Tobacco Merchants 165

This bureau investigated the number of stamps used. During the three-tier tax era, the average number of stamps purchased by British American Tobacco (BAT) calculated from the combined figures issued by the 合基金委員會 (Joint Fund Committee) and the former Unified Tax Bureau for fifteen months was 54,653, while other companies purchased 42,448. Thus, the quantity of cigarettes sold by BAT exceeded that of other companies by 12,205 stamps, meaning BAT accounted for 128% or more of the Chinese merchants' companies, and the Chinese merchants' companies accounted for 77% or more of BAT's sales. During the two-tier tax era, BAT purchased stamps entirely from the former Unified Tax Bureau, with an average of 51,958 stamps for fifteen months, while other tobacco companies purchased 43,582. In this era, BAT's sales exceeded those of other companies by only 8,376 stamps, meaning BAT accounted for 119% or more of the Chinese merchants' companies, and the Chinese merchants' companies accounted for 81% or more of BAT's sales. As for tax payments, during the three-tier tax era, the average amount paid by BAT for fifteen months was 2,410,408 yuan, while other tobacco companies paid 1,904,069 yuan. This indicates that BAT's ability to bear tax burdens was 506,339 yuan more than that of Chinese merchants' companies (i.e., 2,410,408 = 126, 1,904,069 = 100). In the two-tier tax era, the average amount paid by BAT for fifteen months was 2,902,474 yuan, while other tobacco companies paid 2,436,571 yuan, meaning BAT's ability to bear tax burdens was only 465,903 yuan more than that of Chinese merchants' companies (i.e., 2,902,474 = 119, 2,436,571 = 100). Comparing these two tables, the ability of Chinese merchants' companies to bear tax burdens increased, indicating that their operational efficiency improved. Therefore, during the three-tier tax era, the sales volume of Chinese merchants' companies accounted for 77% of BAT's sales. By the two-tier tax era, the sales volume of Chinese merchants' companies had suddenly progressed to account for 81% of BAT's sales. Given that Chinese merchants' companies' operations have shown such progress, the claim that the two-tier tax system hinders the business of Chinese merchants or favors foreign merchants is not an accurate assessment. (4) The original proposal listed errors in the government's unified tax losses. As mentioned above, in the comparison table of stamp usage during the three-tier era in the original submission, the total number of stamps used by BAT was not clearly verified. The 344,239.1 stamps purchased by BAT from the former Unified Tax Bureau, valued at 15,219,592.7 yuan, were mistakenly included in the number of stamps used by the Chinese merchants' companies. The original proposal continued the arguments of the original submission, and its estimation of tax revenue was based on the same fundamental point as the original submission. Therefore, the claim that the government's revenue decreased by 10,068,000 yuan and that Chinese merchants bore an additional burden of 14,520,000 yuan annually after the implementation of the two-tier tax is naturally unfounded. Now, based on the above-mentioned revised detailed table of cigarette stamp sales by grade, this bureau will provide an accurate explanation of the government's tax revenue situation at that time. It was found that during the three-tier tax era, BAT used 54,653 stamps, while during the two-tier tax era, they used 51,958 stamps. Thus, the number of cigarette cases sold by BAT during the two-tier tax era was 2,695 fewer than during the three-tier tax era, a decrease of just over 4%. If the government continued to collect taxes according to the three-tier tax rate, tax revenue would naturally decrease by 4%. BAT's average monthly tax payment during the three-tier tax era was slightly more than 2,410,408 yuan. If calculated based on a 4% decrease, the monthly reduction would inevitably be slightly more than 96,416.32 yuan, meaning BAT's monthly tax payment would only be slightly more than 2,313,991.68 yuan. However, in reality, BAT's average monthly tax payment during the two-tier era reached 2,902,474 yuan. Compared to that era, the government increased tax revenue from BAT by slightly more than 588,482.32 yuan per month, meaning an annual increase of slightly more than 7,061,787.84 yuan. Furthermore, regarding Chinese merchants' companies (i.e., the "other companies" mentioned in the original submission), they used 42,448 stamps during the three-tier tax era and 43,582 stamps during the two-tier tax era. Thus, the number of cigarette cases sold by Chinese merchants' companies during the two-tier tax era increased by just over 2%. If the government continued to collect taxes at the three-tier tax rate, tax revenue should naturally increase by 2%. It was found that the average monthly tax payment of Chinese merchants' companies during the three-tier tax era was 1,904,069 yuan. If calculated based on a 2% increase, it would only increase by slightly more than 38,081.38 yuan, meaning the monthly amount should be slightly more than 1,942,150.38 yuan. However, in reality, the average monthly tax payment of Chinese merchants' companies during the two-tier tax era was 2,436,571 yuan. Compared to that era, Chinese merchants' companies increased their tax payments by slightly more than 494,420.62 yuan per month, meaning a total increase of slightly more than 5,933,047.44 yuan annually. Based on this comprehensive calculation, in the fifteen months after the implementation of the two-tier tax, BAT's tax payment on domestically produced cigarettes increased by 7,061,787.84 yuan, and Chinese merchants' companies' tax payment on domestically produced cigarettes increased by 5,933,047.44 yuan. Considering the cigarette production of both Chinese and foreign factories, the government's tax revenue increased by slightly more than 12,994,835.28 yuan. Thus, there was no loss of government tax revenue for either BAT or Chinese merchants' companies. Considering the increased tax burden, BAT actually bore more than Chinese merchants' companies, and there was no unequal treatment between Chinese and foreign companies. (5) The original submission claimed that 19/20ths of the high-grade cigarettes were produced by BAT and that all of the low-grade cigarettes were produced by Chinese merchants, which is not factual. Regarding the domestically produced cigarettes, whether 19/20ths of the high-grade cigarettes were indeed produced by BAT and whether all of the low-grade cigarettes were produced by Chinese merchants, a correct answer can only be obtained by examining the tax-paid sales volume of all brands of cigarettes produced by manufacturers. Now, based on the most recent fiscal year under the old two-tier tax system, from July 1932 to June 1933, the tax-paid sales volume of cigarettes produced by various Chinese and foreign factories within the unified tax area is listed in order of their registered price tax bracket to form a tentative analysis (attached is a table of tax-paid sales volume of domestically produced cigarettes). Regarding the first-grade cigarettes under the old two-tier system, i.e., cigarettes of various brands with a registered price of 262 yuan or more, the total sales volume of Chinese merchants' companies was slightly more than 11,037 cases, while BAT's total was slightly more than 12,016 cases. This means that when analyzing domestically produced high-grade cigarettes between Chinese merchants and BAT, each accounted for more than 10,000 cases in sales volume, with the difference between Chinese merchants and foreign merchants being only slightly more than 900 cases, or just 9%. Therefore, the original submission's claim that 19/20ths of the high-grade cigarettes were produced by BAT can be proven untrue. Furthermore, regarding second-grade cigarettes, i.e., cigarettes of various brands with a registered price of less than 260 yuan, those priced at 260 yuan had sales of slightly more than 42,275 cases for Chinese merchants and slightly more than 37,470 for BAT; those priced at 250 yuan had sales of slightly more than 18,125 cases for Chinese merchants and only 91 cases for BAT; those priced from 249 yuan down to 240 yuan had sales of slightly more than 5,284 cases for Chinese merchants and only slightly more than 1,824 for BAT; those priced from 239 yuan down to 200 yuan had sales of slightly more than 52,843 cases for Chinese merchants and only slightly more than 8,745 cases for BAT. This means that within the second-tier tax, Chinese merchants dominated cigarettes priced above 200 yuan. However, below 200 yuan, the situation gradually changed, with those priced from 199 yuan to 155 yuan having sales of slightly more than 153,094 cases for Chinese merchants and slightly more than 185,613 for BAT. Furthermore, within the price range from 149 yuan down to 140 yuan, Chinese merchants' sales were only slightly more than 14,581 cases, while BAT's were 20,087 cases, meaning BAT prevailed. Furthermore, within the price range from 139 yuan down to 130 yuan, Chinese merchants' sales were slightly more than 47,208 cases, while BAT's were only 21,004 cases, meaning Chinese merchants prevailed. Furthermore, within the price range from 129 yuan down to 120 yuan, Chinese merchants' sales were slightly more than 117,914 cases, while BAT's were only 93,125 cases, meaning Chinese merchants prevailed again. Therefore, regarding cigarettes priced between 120 yuan and 200 yuan, Chinese merchants and BAT alternately gained and lost, which is a point worth noting. Further down, examining lower-priced cigarettes, those priced between 119 yuan and 110 yuan had only slightly more than 41,364 cases in sales for Chinese merchants, while BAT had as many as 53,170 cases. Furthermore, those priced between 109 yuan and 90 yuan had only slightly more than 22,268 cases in sales for Chinese merchants, while BAT had as many as 51,302 cases. Furthermore, those priced between 89 yuan and 80 yuan had only 2,061 cases in sales for Chinese merchants, while BAT had as many as slightly more than 19,799 cases. Therefore, BAT had more tax-paid sales volume of low-priced cigarettes priced between 80 yuan and 119 yuan. There were also cigarettes priced between 79 yuan and 60 yuan, with Chinese merchants having 1,588 cases and BAT having 54 cases. Sales for both sides were low and statistically insignificant. From the above observation, it can be proven statistically that, in the most recent year after the implementation of the two-tier tax, the sales volume of first-grade cigarettes priced above 260 yuan between Chinese and foreign companies was approximately balanced. Next, analyzing the sales volume of second-grade cigarettes, Chinese merchants sold more of those priced between 260 yuan and 200 yuan. Within the range from 199 yuan down to 129 yuan, sales volume between Chinese and foreign companies still alternately gained and lost, but within the range from 190 yuan down to 80 yuan, BAT alone had higher sales. Therefore, the original submission's claim that 19/20ths of high-grade cigarettes were produced by BAT and that all low-grade cigarettes were produced by Chinese merchants is purely speculative and not credible. As for the original submission using 65 yuan as the representative price for low-grade cigarettes and insisting on using it as the basis for calculating tax brackets, although it has been debated repeatedly, this bureau found that among the Chinese and foreign tobacco merchants who formally reported and registered cigarettes priced at 65 yuan, there were only two brands, one belonging to a Chinese merchant and one belonging to BAT, namely the 20-cigarette pack Fengmei brand from Shanghai Zhida Xinji and the 50-cigarette pack Bagua brand from BAT. However, among the twenty-four companies in the original submission, none produced cigarettes priced at 65 yuan. Furthermore, examining the sales volume, although Zhida Xinji's Fengmei brand was reported and registered, it has not produced a single case to date. According to recent investigations, BAT's Bagua brand has only had 50 cases leave the factory after paying taxes. In total, according to the registration records, there are no fewer than 1,600 cigarette brands in the second tier, and those priced at 65 yuan account for only two and their case numbers are absolutely few. Therefore, from a legal perspective, 65 yuan cannot be taken to represent the cost unit of all low-grade cigarettes, nor can it be used as the standard price for calculating tax brackets. (To be continued)

Organized by China Travel Service Through-Ticketing to Kuling Now in Effect Prices from Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankow to Kuling China Travel Service Dispatches Personnel Along the Way to Provide Assistance 166

The Shanghai Sichuan Road China Travel Service, in cooperation with the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, British-owned Butterfield & Swire, and Jardine Matheson, is now offering through-ticketing to Kuling. The through-ticketing system is now in effect, and regulations for baggage fees have been established. Details are as follows:
